NOTE On the mXT448UD-CCUBHA1 variant device, although up to 640 nodes are available on the matrix, only a maximum of 448 nodes can be used on this device across all enabled touch object instances.

### 4.2 Key Array T15 Object

#### 4.2.1 INTRODUCTION

##### 4.2.1.1 Standard Keys

The Key Array T15 object is used to configure a rectangular array of XY nodes on the mutual capacitance sensor for use as keys. The Key Array T15 object can be used to configure an array of up to 32 keys.

Refer to the relevant device Datasheet for details on the touchscreen layout rules and how the positioning of the Key Array T15 object relates to the positions of the other touch objects.

##### 4.2.1.2 Generic Keys

The Key Array T15 object can be configured to use the Generic Key X and Y lines instead of the Mutual Capacitance X and Y lines. The Generic Key lines effectively provide an additional 3 mutual capacitance nodes that can be used to form a Key Array only.

For the purposes of configuration:

- The single Generic Key X line is treated as being logically located at X32, that is following the standard X lines.

- The 3 Generic Key Y lines are treated as being logically located at Y0 to Y2, that is within the bounds of the standard Y lines. The generic key Y lines thus logically overlap with the standard Y lines.

- The Key Array cannot make use of both Generic Key lines and standard lines, so the maximum size of the Key Array is 3 keys.

Because the generic keys use a single X line,the key numbers are assigned along the \( Y \) axis.

Refer to relevant device Datasheet for more information on the layout of Key Arrays incorporating the Generic Keys.

Note that using the Generic Keys may add extra noise line measurements, which will impact power consumption and timings. It is therefore recommended that, where spare mutual capacitance sense lines are available, the sense lines are used to form a standard Key Array in preference to using the Generic Key lines.

##### 4.2.1.3 Key IDs

For reporting purposes, the key IDs reported in the Key Array T15 message (see "KEYSTATE Field") correspond to the order of the keys in the defined key array. The keys are numbered along the X lines in Y-X order, as defined by the following equation:

\[\text{ Key ID = (Xline - XORIGIN) + ((Yline - YORIGIN) × XSIZE) }\]

For example,for a standard key array of \( 4\mathrm{X} \) by \( 3\mathrm{Y} \) lines,the key IDs are allocated as in Table 4-2.

Note that, because the generic keys use a single X line, the generic keys are effectively numbered along the Y axis (see Table 4-3).

TABLE 4-2: EXAMPLE KEY NUMBERS - STANDARD KEYS 4 X BY 3 Y LINES

<table><tr><td></td><td></td><td colspan="4">X Lines</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td>Xn</td><td>Xn+1</td><td>Xn+2</td><td>Xn+3</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="3">Y Lines</td><td>Ym</td><td>Key 0</td><td>Key 1</td><td>Key 2</td><td>Key 3</td></tr><tr><td>Ym+1</td><td>Key 4</td><td>Key 5</td><td>Key 6</td><td>Key 7</td></tr><tr><td>Ym+2</td><td>Key 8</td><td>Key 9</td><td>Key 10</td><td>Key 11</td></tr></table>

TABLE 4-3: EXAMPLE KEY NUMBERS - GENERIC KEYS 1 X BY 3 Y LINES

X Lines

GKEYX0

<table><tr><td rowspan="3">Y Lines</td><td>GKEYY0</td><td>Key 0</td></tr><tr><td>GKEYY1</td><td>Key 1</td></tr><tr><td>GKEYY2</td><td>Key 2</td></tr></table>

By default, the key IDs correspond to the key numbers of the defined key array. The Key ID Configuration T16 object, if enabled, allows an alternative mapping between the keys and the key IDs to be configured. This allows the Key Array T15 object to report its key states according to the key IDs defined by the Key ID Configuration T16 object. This may be useful, for example, if the user requires standard key IDs to be used across various products.

##### 4.2.1.4 Touch Threshold

The Key Array T15 object has a Touch Threshold (TCHTHR) that defines how large a node's touch delta (that is, Reference minus the signal) must be to qualify as a potential touch detection. The Reference is determined during calibration and adjusted using drift compensation. The Reference is determined by the Key Array T15 DRIFT and DRIFTST fields.

The final detection confirmation uses the Touch Detect Integration as described in the TCHDI field. Larger values for the threshold desensitize nodes since the signal must change more in order to exceed the threshold level. Conversely, lower thresholds make nodes more sensitive.

The setting for TCHTHR for each node depends on the amount of signal swing that occurs when a node is touched. Thicker panels or smaller electrode geometries reduce node gain, that is signal swing from touch. In this case smaller TCHTHR values are required to detect touch.

A Touch Hysteresis (TCHHYST) can also be set for all keys in the key array. Note, however, that this hysteresis is capped at run time to 25% of the current touch threshold for all keys.

It is also possible to configure separate (per-key) thresholds and/or hystereses using Key Thresholds T14 EXTRATHR and/or EXTRAHYST (see Key Thresholds T14 "EXTRATHR[] Fields" and "EXTRAHYST[] Fields").

Other objects can adjust the minimum threshold in specific circumstances. These objects are:

- Noise Suppression T72 - Supplies a minimum touch threshold that desensitizes the Key Array T15 to avoid reporting any detected noise that would be reported as touches (see Section 5.11 "Noise Suppression T72 Object").

- Glove Detection T78 - Adjusts the threshold to allow for glove touches (see Section 5.12 "Glove Detection T78 Object") unless CTRL IGNGLOVEMODE is set (see "CTRL Field").

##### 4.2.1.5 Adjacent Key Suppression Technology

Adjacent Key Suppression (AKS) technology is a patented method used to detect which touch object (Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 or Key Array T15) is touched, and to suppress touches on the other touch objects, when touch objects are located close together.

The device has two levels of AKS:

- The first level works between the touch objects (Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 and Key Array T15). The touch objects are assigned to AKS groups. If a touch occurs within one of the touch objects in a group, then touches within other objects inside that group are suppressed. For example, if a touchscreen and a Key Array are placed in the same AKS group, then a touch in the touchscreen will suppress touches in the Key Array, and vice versa.

A touch in a group of AKS objects is indicated only on the object with the largest signal. This is assumed to be the intended object. Once an object in an AKS group is in detect, there can be no further detections within that group until the object is released.

Objects can be in more than one AKS group.

- The second level of AKS is internal AKS within an individual Key Array object (note that internal AKS is not present on other types of touch objects, only a Key Array T15). If internal AKS is enabled, then when one key is touched, touches on all the other keys within the Key Array are suppressed.

AKS technology works best when it operates in conjunction with a detect integration setting of several acquisition cycles.

NOTE If a touch is in detect and then AKS is enabled, that touch will not be forced out of detect. It will not go out of detect until the touch is released. AKS will then operate normally. This applies to both levels of AKS.

#### 4.2.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 4-4: CONFIGURATION FOR KEY ARRAY T15

(TOUCH_KEYARRAY_T15)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td>INTAKSEN</td><td colspan="2">Reserved</td><td>IGNGLOVEMODE</td><td>TSCONTSUP</td><td>Reserved</td><td>RPTEN</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>XORIGIN</td><td colspan="8">X line start position of object</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>YORIGIN</td><td colspan="8">Y line start position of object</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>XSIZE</td><td colspan="8">Number of X lines the object occupies</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>YSIZE</td><td colspan="8">Number of Y lines the object occupies</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>AKSCFG</td><td>Group8</td><td>Group7</td><td>Group6</td><td>Group5</td><td>Group4</td><td>Group3</td><td>Group2</td><td>Group1</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>GAIN</td><td colspan="8">Measurement gain</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>TCHTHR</td><td colspan="8">Touch threshold</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>TCHDI</td><td>DISTCHDIDOWN</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="6">TCHDI</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>TCHHYST</td><td colspan="2">Reserved</td><td colspan="6">Touch hysteresis</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>CFG</td><td colspan="5">Reserved</td><td>DBGSIGSEN</td><td>DBGREFSEN</td><td>DBGDELTASEN</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables the use of the Key Array T15 object. The object is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0.

RPTEN: Allows the object to send status messages to the host through the Message Processor T5 object. Reporting is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0.

TSCONTSUP: If this bit is set to 1, the Touchscreen Contact Suppression algorithm enabled. When this feature is enabled, key reporting for Key Array T15 will be suppressed if there is a contacting touch on any touchscreen when the keys are going into detect. Key reporting will remain suppressed until all keys are released.

In designs where keys are situated near to the touchscreen without a bezel separation, there is a possibility that the user's touch might unintentionally slide onto a key. Even with AKS enabled, the key can still report, once the touch is no longer detected on the touchscreen. In this case, enabling the Touchscreen Contact Suppression can help suppress the key.

Note that for the Touchscreen Contact Suppression to function, the external AKS (see "AKSCFG Field") between the key array and the touchscreen has to be disabled (that is, they cannot be in the same AKS group).

IGNGLOVEMODE: Ignores Glove Mode. This controls any threshold adjustment relating to gloves. If this bit is set to 0, Glove Detection T78 may lower the Key Array T15 TCHTHR so that gloves may be detected. If this bit is set to 1 (recommended), Glove Detection T78 no longer has any control over the Key Array T15 TCHTHR, but the user may set Key Array T15 TCHTHR to detect gloves explicitly.

Microchip recommends that IGNGLOVEMODE is always set to 1.

INTAKSEN: Enables internal Adjacent Key Suppression® (AKS®) between keys in the array (see Section 4.2.1.5 "Adjacent Key Suppression Technology"). If internal AKS is enabled, then when one key is touched, touches on all the other keys within the Key Array are suppressed. Set this bit to 1 to enable internal AKS, and to 0 to disable internal AKS.

## XORIGIN, YORIGIN, XSIZE and YSIZE Fields

These fields specify the size and position of the key Array on the actual sensor matrix (see Figure 4-1). The XORIGIN and YORIGIN fields specify the origin in X and Y lines. The XSIZE and YSIZE fields specify the size in X/Y nodes (keys).

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_46.jpg?x=510&y=217&w=894&h=533&r=0"/>

The minimum size for an enabled key array is \( 1\mathrm{X} \) by \( 1\mathrm{Y} \) line. The maximum size for a key array is such that when XSIZE and YSIZE are multiplied together they obey the rule: XSIZE * YSIZE ≤ 32 nodes. Setting XSIZE and YSIZE to values that create more than 32 keys causes a configuration error.

NOTE A standard key array must not share X and Y lines with other touch objects (specifically Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100). In addition, the key array must use X and Y lines numbered above those used by the enabled Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object.

Note that this restriction does not apply to a key array that is implemented using the generic keys as they do not use the physical \( X \) and \( Y \) lines on the main sensor.

Refer to the relevant device Datasheet for full details on the layout of the sensor.

XORIGIN Range for Standard Key Array: (T100.XORIGIN + T100.XSIZE) to (maxX – T15.XSIZE + 1)

YORIGIN Range for Standard Key Array: (T100.YORIGIN + T100.YSIZE) to (maxY – T15.YSIZE + 1)

XORIGIN Range for Generic Key Array: 32 only

YORIGIN Range for Generic Key Array: 0 to 2

XSIZE Range for Standard Key Array: 1 to (32 / YSIZE)

YSIZE Range for Standard Key Array: 1 to (32 / XSIZE)

XSIZE Range for Generic Key Array: 1 only

YSIZE Range for Generic Key Array: 1 to 3

## AKSCFG Field

This field configures Adjacent Key Suppression (AKS) between this Key Array T15 object and any other touch objects (see Section 4.2.1.5 "Adjacent Key Suppression Technology").

Group1 to 8: These bits form a bit field that specifies which AKS groups this Key Array is within. The default value of 0 means that the object is in no AKS groups and the AKS feature is disabled for the Key Array.

Range: 0 to 255

## GAIN Field

This field sets the gain of the analog circuits in front of the analog to digital converter (ADC).

Range: 0 to 22

## TCHTHR Field

This field specifies the Touch Threshold in 8-bit deltas (see Section 4.2.1 "Introduction" for details).

NOTE

- The Touch Hysteresis specified in the TCHHYST field also has an effect on the Touch Threshold (See "TCHHYST Field") and should therefore be allowed for in the TCHTHR setting.

- A per-key threshold and/or hysteresis may be configured using Key Thresholds T14 EXTRATHR and/or EXTRAHYST (see Key Thresholds T14 "EXTRATHR[] Fields" and "EXTRAHYST[] Fields").

Range: 0 to 255

## TCHDI Field

To suppress false detections caused by spurious events like electrical noise, the device incorporates a touch detection integrator (DI) counter mechanism to provide signal filtering. A per-key counter is incremented each cycle that a touch is detected. When this counter reaches a preset limit the touch is finally declared to be present. If on any acquisition a delta is not seen to exceed the threshold level, the counter is cleared and the process has to start from the beginning.

The number of cycles for a touch to go into detect depends on the setting of DISTCHDIDOWN:

- If DISTCHDIDOWN = 0, it takes TCHDI + 1 cycles from touchdown to when the first touch is actually reported via the CHG_I2C or CHG_SPI line, with a minimum time of 2 cycles.

However, if DISTCHDIDOWN is set to 0 in the Key Array T15 object, but is set to 1 in any other touch object instance with a DISTCHDIDOWN control (for example, the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object), it takes only TCHDI cycles, with a minimum time of 1 cycle.

Once a touch is detected, the limit is changed to TCHDI cycles.

- If DISTCHDIDOWN = 1, it takes 1 cycle from touchdown to when the first touch is actually reported (that is, TCHDI is ignored).

IMPORTANT! Touch DI must be enabled for UL/IEC 60730 Class B compliance. Therefore the DISTCHDIDOWN must be set to 0 (that is, touch DI must not be disabled).

An opposite process is applied when a key leaves detection. The counter is decremented each cycle that the delta does not exceed the threshold level, and incremented again if it does exceed the threshold. When the counter reaches zero, the touch is finally declared to be out of detect. For TCHDI values of 0 and 1, it takes 1 cycle for a touch to go out of detect; for TCHDI values of 2 to 63 it takes (TCHDI + 1) cycles.

The effects of various TCHDI values, and the DISTCHDIDOWN control, are summarized in Table 4-5 and Table 4-6.

TABLE 4-5: TCHDI - DISTCHDIDOWN = 0

<table><tr><td rowspan="2">Condition</td><td colspan="4">Number of Cycles</td><td rowspan="2">Notes</td></tr><tr><td>TCHDI = 0</td><td>TCHDI = 1</td><td>TCHDI = 2</td><td>TCHDI \( \geq  3 \) (n)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2">First touch down (from Idle)</td><td>2</td><td>2</td><td>3</td><td>\( n + 1 \)</td><td>DISTCHDIDOWN = 0 in all other objects/instances</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>2</td><td>n</td><td>DISTCHDIDOWN = 1 in at least one other object/instance</td></tr><tr><td>Next touch down (from Active)</td><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>2</td><td>n</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Touch release</td><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>3</td><td>\( n + 1 \)</td><td></td></tr></table>

## TABLE 4-6: TCHDI - DISTCHDIDOWN = 1

<table><tr><td rowspan="2">Condition</td><td colspan="4">Number of Cycles</td></tr><tr><td>TCHDI = 0</td><td>TCHDI = 1</td><td>TCHDI = 2</td><td>TCHDI \( \geq  3\left( n\right) \)</td></tr><tr><td>Touch down</td><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>Touch release</td><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>3</td><td>\( n + 1 \)</td></tr></table>

TCHDI: Specifies the base number of DI cycles.

The range for TCHDI is 0 to 63, where 0 is the same as 1.

TCHDI Range: 0 (1), 1 to 63

DISTCHDIDOWN: Disables Detect Integration (DI) Touchdown. When this control is set to 1, the DI process is disabled for touchdown and the value set in the TCHDI control is ignored. The TCHDI control is, however, still used for the DI process on touch release.

NOTE By setting this control to 1, first touch latency will be reduced. This can, however, have a detrimental effect on the reliability of touchdown detection for all touch object instances other than Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100. Microchip therefore recommends setting DISTCHDIDOWN to 0.

## TCHHYST Field

This field sets the Touch Hysteresis (in 8-bit deltas). This is the level of hysteresis applied to touch detections for all keys in the key array. For a touch to enter detection the touch delta must be greater than the touch threshold (TCHTHR). For a touch to leave detection the touch delta must be less than (TCHTHR - TCHHYST). This field allows the Key Array T15 to be tuned so that a hovering finger does not cause detection to flicker on and off.

Note that if the Noise Suppression T72 object supplies a minimum touch threshold that is greater than TCHTHR - TCHHYST, then a touch's delta must be greater than the minimum touch threshold plus TCHHYST to enter detection, and less than the minimum touch threshold to leave detection.

TCHHYST is capped internally to (TCHTHR / 4). A hysteresis greater than 25% of the Touch Threshold is therefore not possible.

NOTE A per-key hysteresis may be configured using Key Thresholds T14 EXTRAHYST (see "EXTRAHYST[] Fields").

Range: 0 (2), 1 to 63

## CFG Field

This field allows different debug data types to be enabled or disabled for use with the hardware debug interface

DBGDELTASEN: If this bit is set to 1, the key deltas are output by the hardware debug interface. Note that the Command Processor T6 DEBUGCTRL2 DBGOBJMODEEN bit must be set to 1 for this to work (see "DEBUGCTRL2 Field").

DBGREFSEN: If this bit is set to 1, the key references are output by the hardware debug interface. Note that the Command Processor T6 DEBUGCTRL2 DBGOBJMODEEN bit must be set to 1 for this to work (see "DEBUGCTRL2 Field").

DBGSIGSEN: If this bit is set to 1, the key signals are output by the hardware debug interface. Note that the Command Processor T6 DEBUGCTRL2 DBGOBJMODEEN bit must be set to 1 for this to work (see "DEBUGCTRL2 Field").

#### 4.2.3 CONFIGURATION CHECKS

The Key Array T15 object causes a configuration check to be performed in the following circumstances:

- When the object is enabled (that is, the ENABLE bit is set in the CTRL field)

- If the object is enabled, when certain fields are changed

In addition, some fields will cause an automatic recalibration to be performed.

A configuration check may determine that a configuration error has occurred (for example, if a setting is set outside of its allowed range or a conflict has occurred between two settings). This is signaled to the host (see Section 3.3 "Command Processor T6 Object"). The device halts until the error has been corrected.

In addition to the configuration errors caused by the field listed in Table 4-7, the following may also cause an error:

- If the defined key array includes both standard matrix keys and generic keys.

- If the Key Arrays uses Generic Keys, XORIGIN or YORGIN is not within the Generic Key region.

- If the Key Arrays uses Generic Keys, a Generic Key pin has an alternative function and that function is being used.

To fix the error, the object settings should be checked to verify that they are all within their allowed limits, as described in the field descriptions. In particular, the following should be checked:

- There are no more than 32 keys defined, that is: XSIZE x YSIZE ≤ 32.

- The key array does not share X and Y lines with other touch objects (specifically Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100). Specifically, the key array must use X and Y lines numbered above those used by the enabled Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object.

- The key array does not straddle both standard sense lines and generic key sense lines.

- If the Generic Key pins (GKEYX0,GKEYY0 to GKEYY2) have alternative functions, the pins are not being used for their alternative functions.

TABLE 4-7: CONFIGURATION CHECKS FOR KEY ARRAY T15 (TOUCH_KEYARRAY_T15)

<table><tr><td rowspan="2">Field</td><td colspan="2">Changing The Field Causes...</td><td rowspan="2">Effect of Configuration Checks On Field</td></tr><tr><td>Configuration Check</td><td>Automatic Recalibration</td></tr><tr><td>CTRL</td><td>Yes (1)</td><td>Yes (1) (2)</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>XORIGIN</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>Error if out of range</td></tr><tr><td>YORIGIN</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>Error if out of range</td></tr><tr><td>XSIZE</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>Error if out of range</td></tr><tr><td>YSIZE</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>Error if out of range</td></tr><tr><td>AKSCFG</td><td>No</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>GAIN</td><td>No</td><td>Yes</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>TCHTHR</td><td>No</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>TCHDI</td><td>No</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>TCHHYST</td><td>No</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>CFG</td><td>No</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr></table>

Note 1: If the ENABLE bit is toggled on or off.

2: If the ENABLE bit is toggled on or off. Note that if the ENABLE bit is cleared and all of the touch objects are now disabled, no calibration takes place.

Note that Key Array T15 messages will be suppressed if Touchscreen Contact Suppression is enabled, and the conditions are met (see TSCONTSUP bit in the "CTRL Field").

## STATUS Field

Reports the current status of the object.

DETECT: Set if any key is in a touched state.

KEYSTATE Field

KEY0 to KEY31: Report the states of each key in the Key Array, one bit per reported Key ID, which by default equals the key number (see Section 4.2.1.3 "Key IDs"). For example, by default, Key0 has a key ID of 0, which is reported in bit 0 of byte 2 . The key state is reported as 0 if the key is untouched, and 1 if the key is touched.

If the Key ID Configuration T16 object is enabled for use (see Section 5.3 "Key ID Configuration T16 Object"), then the key states are reported according to the key IDs configured in the associated Key ID Configuration T16 object. For example, if Key0 is configured in Key ID Configuration T16 to report as Key ID 8, Key0 will be reported in bit 0 of byte 3 (and not in bit 0 of byte 2).

#### 4.2.5 DIAGNOSTIC DEBUG DATA

The diagnostic debug data modes for the Key Array T15 object is shown in Table 4-9. The diagnostic debug data can be viewed in the Diagnostic Debug T37 object by using the appropriate Command Processor T6 command, also listed in Table 4-9.

The debug data is output according to the physical key number, and not according to any mapping of key IDs defined by the Key ID Configuration T16 object. It is therefore the user's responsibility to maintain a record of the Key ID Configuration T16 Key ID mapping information while inspecting the debug data for any Key Array T15 keys. Alternatively, the Key ID Configuration T16 should be disabled while inspecting the debug data.

The diagnostic debug modes are described in the following sections.

### 4.3 Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 Object

#### 4.3.1 INTRODUCTION

The Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object is used to configure a multiple-touch touchscreen on the sensor matrix that

The Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object reports on all measurements made in the region of the sensor matrix that it occupies, including those detected by other linked objects (see Section 4.3.4 "Messages").

NOTE To be able to track and report touches in self capacitance measurements, the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object needs to have data for both axes (see Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 "CTRL Field" and Appendix A "Measurement Processing").

##### 4.3.1.1 Touch Threshold

Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object has a Touch Threshold (TCHTHR) that defines how large a node's touch delta (Reference minus the signal) must be to qualify as a potential touch detection (in 8-bit deltas). The reference level is determined during calibration and adjusted using drift compensation. The final detection confirmation uses the Touch Detect Integration as described in "TCHDIDOWN Field". Larger values for the threshold desensitize nodes, since the signal must change more in order to exceed the threshold level. Conversely, lower thresholds make nodes more sensitive.

The setting for TCHTHR for each node depends on the amount of signal swing that occurs when a node is touched. Thicker panels or smaller electrode geometries reduce node gain, that is signal swing from touch. In this case smaller TCHTHR values are required to detect touch.

A Touch Hysteresis is provided by the TCHHYST field. For a touch to enter detection the touch delta must be greater or equal to the touch threshold (TCHTHR). For a touch to leave detection the touch delta must be less than (TCHTHR - TCHHYST).

In addition to the Touch Threshold there is also an Internal Touch Threshold that operates in a similar manner to control internally tracked touch detections. By default, it is set to (TCHTHR - TCHHYST)/2. The Internal Touch Threshold also has a hysteresis (INTTHRHYST). For a touch, therefore, to enter detection the touch delta must be greater or equal to INTTHR and for a touch to leave detection the touch delta must be less than (INTTHR - INTTHRHYST).

Other objects can adjust the minimum touch threshold in specific circumstances. These objects are:

- Noise Suppression T72 - Supplies a minimum touch threshold that desensitizes the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 to avoid reporting any detected noise that would be reported as touches (see Section 5.11 "Noise Suppression T72 Object"). This affects both the Touch Threshold and the Internal Touch Threshold.

Note that if the Noise Suppression T72 object supplies a minimum touch threshold that is greater than TCHTHR - TCHHYST, then a touch delta must be greater than the minimum touch threshold plus TCHHYST to enter detection, and less than the minimum touch threshold to leave detection.

Similarly, if the Noise Suppression T72 object supplies a minimum touch threshold that is greater than INTTHR - INTTHRHYST, then a touch's delta must be greater than the minimum touch threshold plus INTTHRHYST to enter detection, and less than the minimum touch threshold to leave detection.

- Glove Detection T78 - Can adjust the threshold to allow for glove touches (see Section 5.12 "Glove Detection T78 Object").

##### 4.3.1.2 Edge Correction

The Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object allows edge correction to be applied for improved linearity at the edge of the screen on certain touchscreen designs. The following edge correction functionality is provided (see Table 4-10):

- Uniform edge correction - The edge correction settings are the same for both the high and low sense lines on the \( X \) or \( Y \) axis.

- Separate edge correction - The edge correction settings are different for both the high and low sense lines on the X or Y axis. This allows separate control of the edge correction that is applied to the high and low sense line edges. Sensors with different non-linear responses at the high and low sense lines of a particular axis can therefore be corrected for.

- Dual X - In addition to the uniform and separate edge correction modes, the X axis can have additional settings that apply when Dual X measurements are being made.

The chosen edge correction can also be overridden by other objects for certain types of touches (although edge correction for normal finger touches is still controlled by Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100):

- Passive Stylus T47 - provides edge correction for passive stylus touches (see Section 5.8.2 "Configuration").

Edge correction requires two parameters to be specified: the Distance fields (see Table 4-10), which specify the width of the region at the edge of the sensor where edge corrections are applied, and the Gradient controls, which adjust the "slope" of the corrections within the edge regions specified by the Distance fields.

The edge correction controls operate on the physical ITO matrix of the touchscreen.

The edge correction controls are not affected by the logical orientation set by the orientation controls in the CFG1 field.

The types of edge correction can be set independently on the X and Y axes. For example, it is possible to have uniform edge correction on the Y axis and separate edge correction on the X axis.

See the following sections for more information on the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 fields that control edge correction:

"XEDGECFG, DXXEDGECFG and YEDGECFG Fields"

"XEDGEDIST, DXXEDGEDIST and YEDGEDIST Fields"

"XEDGECFGHI, DXXEDGECFGHI and YEDGECFGHI Fields"

"XEDGEDISTHI, DXXEDGEDISTHI and YEDGEDISTHI Fields"

Detailed information on tuning the edge correction can be found in the following application note:

- Application Note AN2659: Edge Correction on a maXTouch Touch Sensor: an Empirical Method

TABLE 4-10: EDGE CORRECTION FIELDS

<table><tr><td>Setting</td><td>Fields</td><td>Effect</td></tr><tr><td>Uniform X Edge Correction XEDGECFGHI ENABLE = 0</td><td>XEDGECFG XEDGEDIST</td><td>Set the edge correction for both high and low X lines.</td></tr><tr><td>Uniform Dual X Edge Correction DXXEDGECFGHI ENABLE = 0</td><td>DXXEDGECFG <br> DXXEDGEDIST</td><td>Set the edge correction for both high and low X lines for Dual X measurements.</td></tr><tr><td>Uniform Y Edge Correction YEDGECFGHI ENABLE = 0</td><td>YEDGECFG YEDGEDIST</td><td>Set the edge correction for both high and low Y lines.</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2">Separate X Edge Correction XEDGECFGHI ENABLE = 1</td><td>XEDGECFGHI XEDGEDISTHI</td><td>Set the edge correction for high X lines.</td></tr><tr><td>XEDGECFG <br> XEDGEDIST</td><td>Set the edge correction for low X lines.</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2">Separate Dual X Edge Correction DXXEDGECFGHI ENABLE = 1</td><td>DXXEDGECFGHI <br> DXXEDGEDISTHI</td><td>Set the edge correction for high X lines for Dual X measurements.</td></tr><tr><td>DXXEDGECFG DXXEDGEDIST</td><td>Set the edge correction for low X lines for Dual X measurements.</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2">Separate Y Edge Correction YEDGECFGHI ENABLE = 1</td><td>YEDGECFGHI <br> YEDGEDISTHI</td><td>Set the edge correction for high Y lines.</td></tr><tr><td>YEDGECFG <br> YEDGEDIST</td><td>Set the edge correction for low Y lines.</td></tr></table>

Low and high sense lines have same edge correction

Low and high sense lines have different edge correction

Note: Other objects may supply edge correction for specific types of touches, in which case they will take precedence over Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 edge correction settings.

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables the use of the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object. The object is enabled if set to 1 , and disabled if set to 0 . The object does not scan for touches if it is disabled, in order to conserve power.

RPTEN: Allows the object to send status messages to the host through the Message Processor T5 object. Reporting is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0. Events must be enabled for this bit to have an effect.

DISSCRMSG0: Disables the generation of screen messages in the first report ID.

SCANEN: Enables close scanning for touch detections. The device normally has a very efficient mechanism for determining touch separation (that is, distinguishing between multiple fingers). This is sufficient for most purposes. Under some (very unusual) circumstances, however, it is possible for it to fail to distinguish between multiple touches. Setting this bit to 1 causes the device to perform a close scan for touch detections once every \( {200}\mathrm{\;{ms}} \) . Multiple touches are correctly detected, but the checks still occur infrequently enough to prevent excessive power consumption. This scan is done only when the touchscreen is touched.

CFG1 Field

RPTEACHCYCLE: Setting this bit to 1 causes the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object to generate a touch status message at the end of each sensor scan cycle for each touch that is reporting, irrespective of whether any events have happened. The message will have the same touch co-ordinates as the preceding touch status message. Setting this bit to 0 gives the default message generation behavior described in Section 4.3.4.3 "Subsequent Report IDs - Touch Status Messages".

ATCHTHRSEL: Selects whether the Antitouch Threshold for Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 is based on the TCHTHR or INTTHR field. If ATCHTHRSEL is set to 0, the antitouch threshold will be -(TCHTHR-TCHHYST); if ATCHTHRSEL is set to 1, then the antitouch threshold will be -(INTTHR-INTTHRHYST).

This control affects the following features:

- The SCRAUX ATCHAREA data reported in the AUXDATA[] message fields (see "SCRAUX Field" and "AUXDATA[] Fields")

- The Acquisition Configuration T8 mutual capacitance calibration recovery (see Acquisition Configuration T8 Section 3.5.1 "Introduction" and configuration fields)

- The Retransmission Compensation T80 Working Threshold, as determined by the MOISTTHR and MOISTDEGTHR fields (see Section 5.13.1.3 "Working Threshold")

DISLOCK: Disables the coordinate position locking that is applied to touches inside a clipping boundary (see "XRANGE/YRANGE, XLOCLIP/YLOCLIP and XHICLIP/YHICLIP Fields" for more information). Set this field to 1 to disable locking, and to 0 to enable locking.

SWITCHXY: Switches the X and Y positions; that is, the screen is flipped about the diagonal from (0, 0) to (XRANGE, YRANGE).

INVERTY: Inverts Y coordinates; that is: Ynewval = (YRANGE - Y), where Ynewval is the new Y coordinate after the invert operation.

INVERTX: Inverts X coordinates; that is: Xnewval = (XRANGE - X), where Xnewval is the new X coordinate after the invert operation.

Notes:

- The orientation controls are applied to the touchscreen after the resolution has been applied and the position determined (see Figure 4-16 on page 70).

- An INVERTX and/or INVERTY operation takes place before a SWITCHXY.

The effect of these three bits is shown in Table 4-12.

Note: XRANGE and YRANGE refer to the maximum X and Y screen positions; that is, they relate to the touchscreen resolution and not to the device X and Y lines.

## SCRAUX Field

This field configures the report output in the AUXDATA[] fields for the screen status messages (see Section 4.3.4.1 "First Report ID - Screen Status Messages"). See also "SCRAREAHYST Field".

The AUXDATA[] message bytes are filled in the same order as the SCRAUX bits, depending on which bits are enabled. For example, if only the NUMRPTTCH and TCHAREA bits are set in the SCRAUX configuration field, then only AUXDATA[0] to AUXDATA[2] are used (that is, byte for NUMRPTTCH followed by two bytes for TCHAREA). This is summarized in Figure 4-5.

FIGURE 4-5: EXAMPLE SCREEN STATUS MESSAGE

SCRAUX Configuration Field

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_58.jpg?x=350&y=332&w=1199&h=575&r=0"/>

NUMRPTTCH: If this bit is set to 1, the number of reportable touches that are being tracked on the touchscreen will be reported in the AUXDATA[] fields. The AUXDATA[] Fields for NUMRPTTCH are shown in Table 4-13.

TABLE 4-13: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR NUMRPTTCH

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td>NUMRPTTCH</td><td colspan="8">Number of Reportable Touches</td></tr></table>

The NUMRPTTCH message field indicates the number of reportable touches currently on the screen. A screen status message is generated when this value changes.

TCHAREA: If this bit is set to 1, the number of nodes \( \geq \) (TCHTHR - TCHHYST) on the touchscreen will be reported in the AUXDATA[] fields. The AUXDATA[] Fields for TCHAREA are shown in Table 4-14.

TABLE 4-14: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR TCHAREA

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td rowspan="2">TCHAREA</td><td colspan="8">Touch area LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>\( n + 1 \)</td><td colspan="8">Touch area MSByte</td></tr></table>

The TCHAREA message field indicates the total number of nodes with deltas \( \geq \) (TCHTHR - TCHHYST) on the touchscreen. A screen status message is generated when this value changes by more than SCRAREAHYST.

The data reported in TCHAREA is based on data after processing by the Retransmission Compensation T80 object if the Retransmission Compensation T80 object is enabled.

ATCHAREA: If this bit is set to 1, the number of nodes below the antitouch threshold on the touchscreen will be reported in the AUXDATA[] fields (see ATCHTHRSEL in the "CFG1 Field"). The AUXDATA[] Fields for ATCHAREA are shown in Table 4-15.

TABLE 4-15: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR ATCHAREA

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td rowspan="2">ATCHAREA</td><td colspan="8">Antitouch area LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>n + 1</td><td colspan="8">Antitouch Area MSByte</td></tr></table>

The ATCHAREA message field indicates the total number of nodes below the antitouch threshold on the touchscreen. A screen status message is generated when this value changes by more than SCRAREAHYST.

INTTHRAREA: If this bit is set to 1, the number of nodes above (INTTHR -INTTHRHYST) on the touchscreen will be reported in the AUXDATA[] fields. The AUXDATA[] Fields for INTTHRAREA are shown in Table 4-16.

## TABLE 4-16: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR INTTHRAREA

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td rowspan="2">INTTHRAREA</td><td colspan="8">Internal tracking threshold area LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>n+1</td><td colspan="8">Internal tracking threshold area MSByte</td></tr></table>

The INTTHRAREA message field indicates the total number of nodes above (INTTHR -INTTHRHYST) on the touchscreen. A screen status message is generated when this value changes by more than SCRAREAHYST.

The data reported in INTTCHAREA is based on data after processing by the Retransmission Compensation T80 object if the Retransmission Compensation T80 object is enabled.

## TCHAUX Field

This field configures the report output in the AUXDATA[] fields for the touch status messages (see Section 4.3.4.3 "Subsequent Report IDs - Touch Status Messages").

The AUXDATA[] bytes are filled in the same order as the TCHAUX bits (starting from bit 0), depending on which bits are enabled.

Note that the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 auxiliary data for touch messages are only updated when a touch is detected. This means that touch release messages will contain, for example, peak deltas that are above threshold.

For example, if the VECT, AMPL and AREAHW bits are set to 1 in the TCHAUX field, then the AUXDATA[] bytes will contain one byte for the VECT data, followed by one byte for AMPL data and finally two bytes for the AREAHW data. This is summarized in Figure 4-6. Note that the intermediate bits (AREA, HW and PEAK) are set to 0 in this example. The AREA, HW and PEAK data is therefore skipped in the AUXDATA[] bytes.

FIGURE 4-6: EXAMPLE TOUCH STATUS MESSAGE

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_59.jpg?x=263&y=1123&w=1368&h=626&r=0"/>

The AUXDATA[] bytes can hold a maximum of four bytes of data, so if more than four bytes of data is selected in TCHAUX, the data for the most significant TCHAUX bits will not appear. For example, if PEAK is also selected, in addition to the bits selected in Figure 4-6, the resulting data is as shown in Figure 4-7. In this case, there is not enough room in the AUXDATA[] bytes for the AREAHW data so it does not appear.

EXAMPLE TOUCH STATUS MESSAGE - DATA DOES NOT FIT

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_60.jpg?x=262&y=246&w=1377&h=706&r=0"/>

VECT: If this bit is set to 1, the vector calculation will be performed on each touch and reported in the AUXDATA[] fields. If this bit set to 0 , the calculation will not be performed allowing processing time to be minimized.

The AUXDATA[] Fields for VECT are shown in Table 4-17.

TABLE 4-17: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR VECT

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td>VECT</td><td colspan="4">VCOMP1</td><td colspan="4">VCOMP0</td></tr></table>

The VECT message field gives an indication of the orientation of the touch and a confidence level as a vector made up of two signed (two's complement) 4-bit components:

- VCOMP1: ratio of (+X,+Y) to (-X,-Y), representing a diagonal (value: -7 to +7)

- VCOMP0: ratio of X to Y (value: -7 to +7)

The magnitude of the vector represents the confidence. The vector uses the following calculations:

\[\text{ Angle } = {\tan }^{-1}\left( \frac{{vcom}{p}_{1}}{{vcom}{p}_{0}}\right) /2\]

\[\text{ Magnitude } = \sqrt{v{\text{ comp }}_{1}^{2} + v{\text{ comp }}_{0}^{2}}\]

NOTE The touch vector is affected by the orientation of the screen (see "CFG1 Field"). In the example touch directions shown in Table 4-18 the normal orientation is assumed.

Changes to this field do not generate a touch status message; the vector is reported only when another message-triggering event occurs.

TABLE 4-18: TOUCH DIRECTION (NORMAL ORIENTATION ASSUMED)

<table><tr><td colspan="2">TCHVECTOR Field</td><td rowspan="2">Touch Direction</td></tr><tr><td>VCOMP1</td><td>VCOMP0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>Positive</td><td><img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_61.jpg?x=1198&y=390&w=159&h=174&r=0"/></td></tr><tr><td>Negative</td><td>Positive</td><td><img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_61.jpg?x=1200&y=600&w=168&h=171&r=0"/></td></tr><tr><td>Negative</td><td>0</td><td><img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_61.jpg?x=1198&y=810&w=176&h=164&r=0"/></td></tr><tr><td>Negative</td><td>Negative</td><td><img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_61.jpg?x=1200&y=1030&w=182&h=147&r=0"/></td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>Negative</td><td><img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_61.jpg?x=1202&y=1233&w=184&h=146&r=0"/></td></tr><tr><td>Positive</td><td>Negative</td><td><img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_61.jpg?x=1202&y=1435&w=180&h=146&r=0"/></td></tr><tr><td>Positive</td><td>0</td><td><img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_61.jpg?x=1202&y=1623&w=172&h=163&r=0"/></td></tr><tr><td>Positive</td><td>Positive</td><td><img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_61.jpg?x=1200&y=1819&w=168&h=172&r=0"/></td></tr></table>

AMPL: If this bit is set to 1, the amplitude calculation will be performed on each touch and reported in the AUXDATA[] fields. If this bit set to 0, the calculation will not be performed allowing processing time to be minimized. See also "AMPLHYST Field". The AUXDATA[] Fields for AMPL are shown in Table 4-19.

TABLE 4-19: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR AMPL

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td>AMPL</td><td colspan="8">Touch amplitude</td></tr></table>

The AMPL message field reports the touch amplitude (saturated to 8 bits). This is a value that is proportional to the signal delta of the nodes within the touch. This can be used, for example, to extrapolate the size or pressure of the user's finger touch. Touch status messages are generated when the delta change in the value is greater than the Amplitude Hysteresis (see "AMPLHYST Field"). The value of the reported touch amplitude can be scaled by the AMPLCOEFF and AMPLOFFSET fields, which are applied before AMPLHYST (see "AMPLCOEFF Field" and "AMPLOFFSET Field").

AREA: If this bit is set to 1, the area calculation will be performed on each touch and reported in the AUXDATA[] fields. If this bit set to 0 , the calculation will not be performed allowing processing time to be minimized. The AUXDATA[] Fields for AREA are shown in Table 4-20.

TABLE 4-20: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR AREA

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td>AREA</td><td colspan="8">Area</td></tr></table>

The AREA message field reports the size of the touch area in terms of the number of nodes that are covered by the touch and are above (TCHTHR-TCHHYST). For example, the area covered by the touch on the touchscreen in Figure 4-8 is 28 nodes.

FIGURE 4-8: TOUCH AREA

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_62.jpg?x=388&y=1032&w=1056&h=320&r=0"/>

Changes to this field do not generate a touch status message; the touch area is reported only when another message-triggering event occurs.

HW: If this bit is set to 1, the height/width calculation will be performed on each touch and reported using the AUXDATA[] fields. Note that the calculation of the height and width uses the XPITCH and YPITCH values and so will be accurate only if these are set correctly for the sensor. If this bit set to 0 , the calculation may not be performed, allowing processing time to be minimized.

The AUXDATA[] Fields for HW are shown in Table 4-21.

TABLE 4-21: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR HW

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td>HEIGHT</td><td colspan="8">Touch height</td></tr><tr><td>n+1</td><td>WIDTH</td><td colspan="8">Touch width</td></tr></table>

The HEIGHT field reports the height of the touch in mm.

The WIDTH field reports the width of the touch in mm.

PEAK: If this bit is set to 1, the peak calculation will be performed on each touch and reported in the AUXDATA[] fields. If this bit set to 0 , the calculation will not be performed allowing processing time to be minimized. The AUXDATA[] Fields for PEAK are shown in Table 4-22.

TABLE 4-22: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR PEAK

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td>PEAK</td><td colspan="8">Peak delta</td></tr></table>

The PEAK message field reports the peak delta of the touch in 8-bit delta units (saturated to 8 bits). Changes to this field do not generate a touch status message; the peak delta is reported only when another message-triggering event occurs.

AREAHW: If this bit is set to 1, the area and height/width calculations will be performed on each touch and the data reported in the AUXDATA[] fields. If this bit set to 0, the calculations may not be performed (allowing processing time to be minimized) and the data will not be reported.

The AREAHW bit can be used to allow more pieces of auxiliary data to be reported at once (for example, area, height and width can be reported at the same time as VECT and AMPL). There is no point in setting AREAHW at the same time as AREA or HW as the same information will be reported in two different ways.

The AUXDATA[] Fields for AREAHW are shown in Table 4-23.

TABLE 4-23: AUXDATA[] FIELDS FOR AREAHW

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>n</td><td>AREAHW[0]</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="2">EXP</td><td colspan="5">AREA</td></tr><tr><td>n + 1</td><td>AREAHW[1]</td><td colspan="4">WIDTH</td><td colspan="4">HEIGHT</td></tr></table>

The AREAHW[0] EXP is an exponent (shift) which applies to AREAHW[0] AREA, AREAHW[1] HEIGHT and AREAHW=[1] WIDTH. For example, EXP can be used to extract the touch area from AREAHW[0], as follows:

Touch Area = AREAHW[0] AREA << AREAHW[0] EXP

After the exponent has been applied, the units of area are nodes and the units of height and width are mm.

If the exponent reaches its maximum value then the reported values in AREAHW[0] AREA, AREAHW[1] HEIGHT and AREAHW[1] WIDTH will be saturated to their respective bit widths.

See AREA on page 63 and HW on page 63 for further information about the reported data.

Changes to the AREAHW bit do not generate a touch status message; the AREAHW data is reported only when another message-triggering event occurs.

## TCHEVENTCFG Field

This field provides secondary configuration options to configure the touch events that are able to cause touch status messages to be generated (see Section 4.3.4.3 "Subsequent Report IDs - Touch Status Messages").

DISDOWN: If this bit is set to 1, the touch DOWN event will not generate a touch message.

DISUP: If this bit is set to 1 , the touch UP event will not generate a touch message.

DISUNSUP: If this bit is set to 1, the touch UNSUP event will not generate a touch message.

DISSUP: If this bit is set to 1, the touch SUP event will not generate a touch message.

DISMOVE: If this bit is set to 1, the touch MOVE event will not generate a touch message.

## AKSCFG Field

This field configures Adjacent Key Suppression (AKS) between this Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 instance and any other touch present on the device.

AKS technology is a patented method used to detect which instance of a touch object is touched when objects are located close together. The touch object instances are assigned to AKS groups (objects can be in more than one AKS group). If a touch occurs within one of the touch objects in a group, then touches within other objects inside that group are suppressed and there can be no further detections within that group until that object instance is released. Note that the touch is indicated on the object with the largest signal and this is assumed to be the intended object instance. See also Section 4.2.1.5 "Adjacent Key Suppression Technology".

GROUP1 to GROUP8: These bits form a bit field that specifies which AKS groups this Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object is within. The default value of 0 means that the object is in no AKS groups and the AKS feature is disabled for the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100.

## NUMTCH Field

The Number of Touches (NUMTCH) setting indicates the number of touches to be reported. Report IDs are not removed (see Section 1.5.6 "Report IDs"). The upper limit for this field is the maximum number of touches (16 on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family).

Touch IDs are allocated sequentially as touches are detected and any Touch IDs below NUMTCH are reported. This means that Touch IDs \( \geq \) NUMTCH are not reported,even if the number of touches currently on the touchscreen does not exceed NUMTCH.

Range: 0 to 16

## XYCFG Field

This field configures settings related to the physical layout of a touchscreen sensor in both axes.

XSPAN and YSPAN: These bits enable the use of an "extra electrode" in the creation of the touch coordinates. XSPAN/YSPAN should be set to 1 if the first and last pixels of the LCD are outside the center point of the first and last sense electrodes.

The XSPAN control applies to the low X and high X edges of the touchscreen, and the YSPAN control applies to the low Y and high Y edges of the touchscreen.

At the edges of a touchscreen sensor pattern there should ideally be a half-width electrode. Depending on how the screen has been designed, there may actually be an electrode that is somewhere between 50 percent and 100 percent width at the edge. This can cause discrepancies between the physical touch position and the reported touch position. XSPAN/YSPAN helps correct these discrepancies.

The XSPAN/YSPAN field is used in combination with XLOCLIP/YLOCLIP and XHICLIP/YHICLIP settings. This allows the device to correct for accuracy or linearity problems resulting from the practicalities of the ITO design.

XSPAN/YSPAN moves the theoretical 0 and XRANGE/YRANGE position outwards from the screen center by one half electrode width each. The XLOCLIP/YLOCLIP and XHICLIP/YHICLIP controls can then be used to move the theoretical 0 and XRANGE/YRANGE position back in towards the center in finer steps.Figure 4-9 shows an example of how to correct for two touchscreen designs with an X size of 14. Note that although Figure 4-9 shows the XSPAN control for the X lines, the same principles apply when the YSPAN bit is used with the Y lines.

FIGURE 4-9: TOUCHSCREEN CORRECTION USING XSPAN CONTROL

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_64.jpg?x=326&y=1140&w=1226&h=824&r=0"/>

## XSIZE and YSIZE Fields

The XSIZE and YSIZE fields specify the size of the touchscreen on the actual matrix in terms of the number of X and Y lines that the touchscreen occupies.

The position of the touchscreen is determined by the XORIGIN and YORIGIN fields (see "XORIGIN and YORIGIN Fields").

For a touchscreen the XSIZE and YSIZE fields should be set as follows (see Figure 4-10):

- XSIZE has a minimum value of 3. If Dual X Drive is enabled for use in the Noise Suppression T72 object, the minimum XSIZE is increased to 4. If self capacitance measurements are enabled in the Acquisition Configuration T8 object on a device where maximum X > maximum Y, the minimum is increased to 6.

- YSIZE has a minimum value of 3.

- The maximum size for a Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 depends on the number of X and Y lines on a particular device. On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family the maximum XSIZE is 32 and the maximum YSIZE is 20.

Refer to the relevant device Datasheet for more information on the layout and configuration of the touchscreen sensor.

## FIGURE 4-10: SIZE AND ORIGIN FIELDS

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_65.jpg?x=532&y=908&w=872&h=493&r=0"/>

Note 1: XORIGIN and YORIGIN must be 0.

2: Xmax and Ymax equal the highest X and Y lines (that is, X31 and Y19 on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family).

XSIZE Range: 3 to 32 or

4 to 32 if Dual X Drive enabled or

6 to 32 if self capacitance measurements enabled

YSIZE Range: 3 to 20

## XORIGIN and YORIGIN Fields

The XORIGIN and YORIGIN fields specify the position of the touchscreen on the actual matrix in terms of the index of the X or Y line of the origin (see Figure 4-10). Note that the size of the touchscreen is specified by the XSIZE and YSIZE fields.

XORIGIN Range: 0 only

YORIGIN Range: 0 only

## XPITCH and YPITCH Fields

These fields specify the physical pitch of the X and Y lines on the touchscreen; that is, the spacing between the centers of the X or Y lines. These settings are specified in units of \( {0.1}\mathrm{\;{mm}} \) ,where a setting of zero means \( 5\mathrm{\;{mm}} \) . These fields allow the touch suppression algorithms to be tuned to non-standard pitch sizes.

Range: 0 (5 mm), 1 to 255

## XRANGE/YRANGE, XLOCLIP/YLOCLIP and XHICLIP/YHICLIP Fields

These six fields control the resolution, and thus the reported position, of the touchscreen.

NOTE The XRANGE/YRANGE, XLOCLIP/YLOCLIP and XHICLIP/YHICLIP fields operate on the base touchscreen layout, and are not affected by the logical orientation set by the orientation controls in the CFG1 field.

The XRANGE and YRANGE fields set the output resolution for the reported position.

The minimum resolution is:

\( \left( {R \times  N}\right) /{256} \)

The maximum resolution is:

\( \left( {R \times  N}\right)  - 2\; \) (capped to 65534)

where:

For XRANGE

R = 1024 - XLOCLIP - XHICLIP

N = XSIZE - 1 + XSPAN_ENABLED

For YRANGE:

R = 1024 - YLOCLIP - YHICLIP

N = YSIZE - 1 + YSPAN_ENABLED

A setting of 0 (default) sets the resolution to 1024. These fields allow a position on the touchscreen to match the resolution of an LCD resolution. For example, to set up a touchscreen to match an LCD with a resolution of 800 x 600, XRANGE and YRANGE would be set to 799 and 599 respectively.

NOTE The maximum allowed value for XRANGE/YRANGE is 65534.

The XLOCLIP/YLOCLIP and XHICLIP/YHICLIP fields set up a clipping boundary (illustrated by the dark gray regions in Figure 4-11 and Figure 4-12). Any touch position within this boundary has its X or Y coordinate clipped to the minimum or maximum value. These fields take a signed (two's complement) 8-bit value, allowing settings in the range -128 to +127. These fields work at 10-bit resolution (that is, a touchscreen range of 1023). This means that the maximum clipping values allow a clipping boundary one eighth of the screen width or height.

Positive values increase the size of the clipping boundary, moving the 0 and XRANGE/YRANGE reported positions further inside the screen (see Figure 4-11). If the touch enters the clipping boundary, the coordinates are locked at the point at which the touch entered the region. The coordinates are updated only when the touch leaves the clipping boundary. This coordinate locking can be disabled using the DISLOCK field.

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_67.jpg?x=423&y=212&w=1069&h=702&r=0"/>

Negative values stretch the 0 and XRANGE/YRANGE positions outside of the screen (see Figure 4-12). This limits the reported minimum and maximum value.

FIGURE 4-12: NEGATIVE CLIPPING BOUNDARY

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_67.jpg?x=305&y=1055&w=1291&h=911&r=0"/>

Adjusting the clipping boundary modifies the accuracy of the reported positions. For example, if the touchscreen is smaller than the physical LCD or is not aligned with the LCD, a combination of positive and negative clipping boundaries help align the reported zero point with the zero point of the LCD. An example of this is shown in Figure 4-13.

FIGURE 4-13: EXAMPLE RESOLUTION FIELDS

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_68.jpg?x=371&y=285&w=1195&h=632&r=0"/>

This example results in the coordinates shown in Figure 4-14. The coordinate mapping is shown in Figure 4-15.

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_68.jpg?x=249&y=1010&w=1322&h=561&r=0"/>

FIGURE 4-15: EXAMPLE RESOLUTION FIELDS - MAPPING OF REPORTED POSITIONS

Reported Position
