### 6.2 Self Test Control T10 Object

#### 6.2.1 INTRODUCTION

The Self Test Control T10 object controls the self-test routines in the device to find faults in the device.

The following objects are associated with the Self Test Control T10 object to provide any configuration data that is used by the tests:

- Self Test Pin Faults T11 - provides configuration data for the Pin Fault tests (see Section 6.3 "Self Test Pin Faults T11 Object")

- Self Test Signal Limits T12 - provides configuration data for the Signal Limit tests (see Section 6.4 "Self Test Signal Limits T12 Object")

The Self Test Control T10 object controls the following types of tests:

- Pre-Operation Self Test (POST) - A set of safety-related tests run at start-up. See Section 6.2.1.1 "Pre-Operation Self Test (POST)" for details.

- Built-In Self Test (BIST) - A set of safety-related tests run in the background when time permits. See Section 6.2.1.2 "Built-In Self Test (BIST)" for details.

- On Demand - Some tests can be run on demand using the CMD field (see "CMD Field") and the results reported immediately to the host. See Section 6.2.1.3 "On Demand Tests" for details.

NOTE A GPIO output can be used to indicate a successful BIST test in addition to Self Test Control T10 messages. This provides heartbeat ("alive") functionality and is toggled at the same frequency as the BIST message. A suitable GPIO pin must be set up as an output (see GPIO Configuration T19 "TRIGGER[] Fields").

In order to comply with IEC60730 Class B requirements, the host must provide suitable verification that the chosen GPIO output is working correctly.

##### 6.2.1.1 Pre-Operation Self Test (POST)

Pre-Operation Self Test (POST) testing can be scheduled to run at system start up. See Section 6.2.1.4 "Self Test Groups" for a list of available tests.

Most of the tests are completed before the reset message is sent to the host and touch processing starts, but some tests require touch processing to be running before they can be carried out. These tests will be completed as soon as possible once touch processing is running.

Once all the POST tests have been finished, the Self Test Control T10 object sends a message to the host to indicate that all the POST tests have completed successfully. If a failure occurs during a test, this will be reported immediately to the host through a Self Test Control T10 test failure message. Some critical failures, however, cannot trigger Self Test Control T10 test failure message, as the device is unable to function correctly (for example, a CPU or memory failure). In these cases, the firmware will reset the device and the resulting communications failure will indicate to the host that a failure has occurred.

NOTE If the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object is disabled during start-up, it may result in some of the dependent POST tests remaining stuck. It is recommended, therefore, to ensure that the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object is always enabled.

##### 6.2.1.2 Built-In Self Test (BIST)

Built-In Self Test (BIST) testing is scheduled to run in the background at regular intervals when time permits. See Section 6.2.1.4 "Self Test Groups" for a list of available tests.

BIST testing does not start until POST testing is complete, and is temporarily suspended while an on-demand test request is serviced. A new cycle of BIST testing is scheduled regularly at the rate defined by TESTINTERVAL (see "TESTINTERVAL Field") and will run in the time available after touch and other higher priority processing.

If there are no failures, a message is sent to the host to indicate that all the BIST tests in the current test cycle have passed and that the product is working correctly. This success message is sent at the rate defined by RPTINTERVAL (see "RPTINTERVAL Field") while there are no test failures. If an "alive" output has also been configured in the GPIO Configuration T19 object, then the output will also change state (toggle) each time the BIST Tests Passed message is sent.

If a failure is detected during the tests, the BIST tests passed message will stop and will not start again until a BIST test cycle has completed without any failures.

If a BIST test cycle has not completed within the time defined by OVERRUNTIME (see "OVERRUNTIME Field"), then a BIST Overrun message is sent to the host. Note that all the tests are still run to completion and will report failures or the BIST tests passed message, as appropriate.

Critical test failures will result in the device being reset. Other failures will each be reported to the host through a Self Test Control T10 test failure message, which is sent as soon as the failure is detected. For a permanent failure, the message will continue to be reported every BIST test cycle, and therefore repeated at the rate defined by TESTINTERVAL.

The time taken to run the BIST tests will depend on how much time is available after high priority touch processing has run compared with the cycle time defined by Power Configuration T7 IDLEACQINT and ACTVACQINT (see "IDLEACQINT and ACTVACQINT Fields"). BIST processing will fill any time remaining in the T7 cycle period after the high priority touch processing has finished.

Each time the BIST processing runs, it will run for a minimum time defined by MINTSTTIMEPERCYC (see "MINTSTTIMEPERCYC Field"). If there is less than the minimum time available before the high priority touch processing expects to run again, then the high priority touch processing will be delayed until the minimum period is complete.

If critical touch processing needs to be run urgently (for example, DI cycles), this takes priority and the minimum BIST time (MINTSTTIMEPERCYC) is ignored, so that no BIST testing is performed during that time slot. However, the minimum can only be ignored for a certain number of consecutive touch processing cycles, as defined by MAXHOLDOFF (see "MAXHOLDOFF Field"). Once the MAXHOLDOFF count has been reached, the minimum BIST time will be applied regardless of the touch processing requirements, and touch processing will be delayed. Note that if MAXHOLDOFF = 0, there is no Hold-off period and the minimum BIST time is applied.

The interplay between the MINTSTTIMEPERCYC and MAXHOLDOFF fields therefore allows the BIST test scheduling to be finely tuned. Recommended initial settings are MINTSTTIMEPERCYC ≥ 40 and MAXHOLDOFF = Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 TCHDIDOWN + 2.

IMPORTANT! The MINTSTTIMEPERCYC and MAXHOLDOFF configuration fields need to be carefully tuned. Care must be taken to ensure that sufficient time is allocated to the BIST processing so that the completion of a BIST test cycle can be guaranteed to be within a BIST test interval. Apparent failures such as "keep alive" messages not being generated may be symptoms of the BIST time parameters being set too aggressively.

If a Signal Limit or CTE BIST test (only) is unavailable to run, the test is skipped for the current test cycle and the test is retried in the next test cycle.

The interleaving of BIST and higher priority processing is shown in Figure 6-1. This shows the scheduling in a normal idle or active touch processing cycle, and the effect of DI cycles and the operation of MAXHOLDOFF.

## FIGURE 6-1: BIST PROCESSING SCHEDULING

Normal Touch Processing Cycle

Touch DI with Self Test T10 MAXHOLDOFF = 2

##### 6.2.1.3 On Demand Tests

Some tests can be run on demand and the results reported immediately to the host. These tests can be requested once POST testing has finished and they take priority over touch processing. BIST is suspended while the on-demand test is carried out and resumes again once the on-demand test has finished.

An on-demand test can be carried out by writing the appropriate command value to the CMD field (see "CMD Field").

See Section 6.2.1.4 "Self Test Groups" for details of which tests can be run in this way.

If one or more on-demand tests are run (either individually or by using the "Run all on-demand tests" command; see "CMD Field"), one or more of the following messages will be sent to the host:

- Test Unavailable - Sent to the host when the application reports that the requested test is unavailable. If more than one test is unavailable, there will be a message for each unavailable test.

- Test Failed - Sent to the host when the application reports that a requested test has failed. Only one such message will be sent: any "Run all on-demand tests" command is terminated as soon as a failure occurs.

- All Tests Passed - One message only is sent to the host after all the tests have finished, if at least one test reported passed.

Note that, in the case of the "Run all on-demand tests" command, if a Test Unavailable message is sent, this applies to only one individual test. The other tests will still continue to run and report as required, including further Test Unavailable messages, a Test Failed message, or an All Tests Passed message.

NOTE The Signal Limit test is the only on-demand test that can be reported as unavailable.

##### 6.2.1.4 Self Test Groups

Table 6-2 lists the self tests available on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family.

TABLE 6-2: SELF TEST GROUPS

Forced reset or Fail Message (Test Code: 3)</td></tr><tr><td>RAM</td><td>CTE RAM: Yes AVR RAM: Automatically tested at start-up</td><td>Yes</td><td>-</td><td>Depends on test. Forced reset or Fail Message (Test Code: 4)</td></tr><tr><td>Power</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>Depends on test. Forced reset or Fail Message (Test Code: 7) (1)</td></tr><tr><td colspan="5">Self Tests for CTE and Touch System Operation</td></tr><tr><td>CTE (Capacitive Touch Engine)</td><td>Yes (2)</td><td>Yes (2)</td><td>-</td><td>Fail Message (Test Code: 5)</td></tr><tr><td>Pin Faults</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>Fail Message (Test Code: 8)</td></tr><tr><td>Signal Limits</td><td>Yes (2)</td><td>Yes (2)</td><td>Yes</td><td>Fail Message (Test Code: 6)</td></tr></table>

Note 1: If a power supplies fails during power on, the device may remain in bootloader mode instead.

2: If the Driven Shield Signal Limit test is enabled in Self Test Signal Limits T12, both the CTE and the Signal Limit tests include additional tests on the Driven Shield (DS0 pin). See Section 6.4.1.2 "Driven Shield Signal Limits Test" for more details.

The self tests are grouped into the following test groups, as listed below. The test groups can be run as POST and/or BIST tests. Note, however, that the CPU test group POST processing is compulsory and is always run automatically at start-up. In addition, the Power, Pin Fault and Signal Limit test groups can also be run using direct commands (see "CMD Field".

## SELF TESTS FOR INTERNAL SYSTEM OPERATION

- CPU - Tests the CPU registers.

- Internal Interrupts - Tests the interrupt latency and handlers in the device.

- Clock - Tests the clocks and timers.

- Flash Memory - Tests the validity of the data in flash memory.

- RAM - Tests the RAM.

- Power - Tests that analog (AVdd), XVdd, and digital I/O (VddIO) power supplies are within their expected ranges. It also tests the brown-out (BOD) detectors. The Power tests can be enabled for both POST and BIST processing, if enabled by the appropriate PWREN bit.

Note that the possibility of receiving a POST power fail message is small because, if there is a power fail at start up, the bootloader will not allow the application (and thereby the POST tests) to run. A POST power failure is reported only if it occurs after the application starts and before the POST power test runs.

If Self Test Control T10 is enabled, and reporting is also enabled, any spurious voltage drop of the power supplies that is detected by the system at runtime will cause the Self Test Control T10 object to generate an automatic "Power Fault" message. For this to happen, however, BIST must be enabled for power tests (BISTCFG PWREN = 1).

NOTE Power Configuration T7 must be configured to allow continuous power monitoring in order for this test to operate (that is, Power Configuration T7 CFG DISPOWMON = 0; see Power Configuration T7 "CFG Field"). Note also that the Power Monitor checks the power supply every cycle, regardless of BIST scheduling.

## SELF TESTS FOR CTE AND TOUCH SYSTEM OPERATION

- CTE - Tests the Capacitive Touch Engine (CTE).

If the Driven Shield Signal Limit test is enabled (see Self Test Signal Limits T12 "CTRL Field"), the CTE tests also validate the CTE measurements performed on the DS0 pin. This allows open pin faults on the DS0 pin to be detected by the signal Limit tests (see below).

- Pin Fault - Tests the sense pins (X0 to X31 and Y0 to Y19), and the Generic Key pins (GKEYX0 and GKEYY0 to GKEYY2), on the device. This test module also tests for shorts on the driven shield pin (DS0). This allows low-resistance shorts (line-to-line, line-to-power and line-to-GND) to be detected, as well as resistive line-to-line shorts. The pin fault tests are configured using the Self Test Pin Faults T11 object (see Section 6.3 "Self Test Pin Faults T11 Object".

- Signal Limit - Tests the signal limits for all measurement types. These test the signals from each of the touch objects on the device. These tests are run for each enabled touch object rather than for the entire touchscreen sensor matrix. Note that Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 must be enabled for the tests to run successfully. The user must specify the expected minimum and maximum level for each touch object under test. The signal limit tests are configured using the Self Test Signal Limits T12 object (see Section 6.4 "Self Test Signal Limits T12 Object").

If the Driven Shield Signal Limits test is enabled (see Self Test Signal Limits T12 "CTRL Field"), the Signal Limit tests also test the DS0 pin. This allows open circuit faults on the DS0 pin to be detected.

Note that Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 CTRL DISMEASX must also be set to 0 if the Driven Shield Signal Limits test is enabled.

NOTE For free-form (non rectangular) screens, it is possible to use the Ignore Nodes T141 and Ignore Nodes Controller T145 objects to indicate that certain nodes are to be ignored by the signal limit test. See Section 5.16 "Ignore Nodes T141 Object" and Section 6.22 "Ignore Nodes Controller T145 Object" for more details.

#### 6.2.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-3: CONFIGURATION FOR SELF TEST CONTROL T10 (SPT_SELFTESTCONTROL_T10)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td>POSTEN</td><td>BISTEN</td><td colspan="4">Reserved</td><td>RPTEN</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>CMD</td><td colspan="8">Test command</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td rowspan="2">POSTCFG</td><td>PWREN</td><td>SIGLIMEN</td><td>CTEEN</td><td>RAMEN</td><td>FLASHEN</td><td>CLOCKEN</td><td>INTSEN</td><td>Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td colspan="7">Reserved</td><td>PINFLTEN</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td rowspan="2">BISTCFG</td><td>PWREN</td><td>SIGLIMEN</td><td>CTEEN</td><td>RAMEN</td><td>FLASHEN</td><td>CLOCKEN</td><td>INTSEN</td><td>CPUEN</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td colspan="7">Reserved</td><td>PINFLTEN</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>TESTINTERVAL</td><td colspan="8">BIST interval</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>MINTSTTIMEPERCYC</td><td colspan="8">Minimum test duration per BIST processing cycle</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>MAXHOLDOFF</td><td colspan="8">Maximum BIST hold-off count</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>OVERRUNTIME</td><td colspan="8">BIST overrun</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>RPTINTERVAL</td><td colspan="8">BIST report interval</td></tr></table>

CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables the use of the Self Test Control T10 object. The object is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0 .

RPTEN: Allows the object to send status messages to the host through the Message Processor T5 object. Reporting is enabled if set to 1 , and disabled if set to 0 .

BISTEN: Enables Built-In Self Test (BIST) processing. The specific tests to be run during BIST processing must be enabled using the BISTCFG field (see "POSTCFG and BISTCFG Fields").

POSTEN: Enables Pre-Operation Self Test (POST) processing. The specific tests to be run during POST processing must be enabled using the POSTCFG field (see "POSTCFG and BISTCFG Fields").

## CMD Field

This field is used to send test commands to the device. Valid test commands are listed in Table 6-4.

TABLE 6-4: TEST COMMANDS

<table><tr><td>Command</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>0x00</td><td>No command</td></tr><tr><td>0x31</td><td>Run the Power test</td></tr><tr><td>0X32</td><td>Run the Pin Fault test</td></tr><tr><td>0x33</td><td>Run the Signal Limit test</td></tr><tr><td>0x3E</td><td>Run all the tests in the order above</td></tr><tr><td>All other values</td><td>Reserved; no effect</td></tr></table>

When the CMD field is set to the code of the test to be run, the Self Test Control T10 object runs the test once and then stops. At the end of the test, the CMD field is cleared to zero. If reporting is enabled (see the "CTRL Field" field), the Self Test Control T10 object also sends a report message with the result of the test (see Section 6.2.3 "Messages").

## POSTCFG and BISTCFG Fields

These fields enable the various types of test available during POST or BIST testing. A test is enabled if a control is set to 1 and disabled if the control is set to 0 .

CPUEN: Enables CPU register BIST tests.

Note that the CPU register POST tests are compulsory and therefore there is no corresponding control to enable or disable it.

INTSEN: Enables Interrupt POST or BIST tests.

CLOCKEN: Enables Clock POST or BIST tests.

FLASHEN: Enables Flash Memory POST or BIST tests.

RAMEN: Enables RAM POST or BIST tests.

CTEEN: Enables CTE POST or BIST tests.

SIGLIMEN: Enables Signal Limit POST or BIST tests.

Note that if the Driven Shield Signal Limit test is enabled (see Self Test Signal Limits T12 "CTRL Field"), the Signal Limit tests also include tests for signal limits on the DS0 pin.

PWREN: Enables Power POST or BIST tests. Power Configuration T7 must be configured to allow continuous power monitoring in order for this test to operate (that is, Power Configuration T7 CFG DISPOWMON = 0; see Power Configuration T7 "CFG Field").

PINFLTEN: Enables Pin Fault POST or BIST tests.

## TESTINTERVAL Field

This field specifies the BIST Test Interval. This is the interval at which the BIST test cycles are started. All enabled BIST tests are run in each BIST test cycle.

The interval is specified in units of \( {50}\mathrm{\;{ms}} \) ,meaning a maximum time of \( {12750}\mathrm{\;{ms}} \) can be specified. The default value of 0 means start a BIST test cycle every measurement processing cycle (as defined by Power Configuration T7 IDLEACQINT/ACTVACQINT; see "IDLEACQINT and ACTVACQINT Fields").

Range: 0 (every processing cycle), 1 to 255

## MINTSTTIMEPERCYC Field

This field specifies the minimum allocated test time (in units of \( {20\mu }\mathrm{s} \) ) per BIST test cycle. This is the minimum amount of time allocated to run the BIST tests in each normal measurement processing cycle. Where possible, the BIST test processing will make use of any available spare time before other processing is scheduled.

This field should be used in conjunction with the MAXHOLDOFF field. See Section 6.2.1.2 "Built-In Self Test (BIST)" for more information.

The Minimum Cycle Duration is specified in units of \( {20\mu }\mathrm{s} \) ,allowing for a minimum duration up to \( {5.1}\mathrm{\;{ms}} \) .

Range: 0 to 255

Typical: \( \geq  {40} \)

## MAXHOLDOFF Field

This field specifies the Maximum Hold-off Count for BIST processing. See Section 6.2.1.2 "Built-In Self Test (BIST)" for more information on how this field is used, and its association with the MINTSTTIMEPERCYC field.

The MAXHOLDOFF field needs to be carefully tuned in conjunction with MINTSTTIMEPERCYC to ensure that sufficient time is allocated to the BIST processing. Recommended initial settings are MINTSTTIMEPERCYC ≥ 40 and MAXHOLDOFF = Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 TCHDIDOWN + 2.

The default value of 0 means no Maximum Hold-off Count, resulting in no Hold-off period.

Range: 0 (no maximum hold off count), 1 to 255

Typical: Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 TCHDIDOWN + 2

## OVERRUNTIME Field

This field defines the BIST Overrun Time. This is the maximum time allowed for a BIST test cycle. If this time is exceeded, a message reporting a BIST cycle overrun is sent to the host.

The BIST Overrun Time is defined in units of 50 ms, thus allowing a maximum time of 12.75 seconds. The default value of 0 means use the time defined for the BIST test interval (see "TESTINTERVAL Field").

Range: 0 (use TESTINTERVAL), 1 to 255

## RPTINTERVAL Field

This field defines the Report Interval. This is the time between sending each BIST test OK message. A GPIO pin can also be toggled (that is, if it is high then set it low, and if it is low then set it high) at the same frequency if a GPIO Configuration T19 GPIO trigger is configured (see GPIO Configuration T19 "TRIGGER[] Fields").

See Section 6.2.1.2 "Built-In Self Test (BIST)" for a detailed description. The report interval is specified in units of 50 ms, meaning a maximum time of 12.75 seconds can be specified. The default value of 0 means every processing cycle (see Power Configuration T7 "IDLEACQINT and ACTVACQINT Fields").

Range: 0 (every processing cycle), 1 to 255

#### 6.2.3 MESSAGES

The Self Test Control T10 object reports the success or failure of POST, BIST and on-demand tests in its message data. In addition, if a BIST test cycle has not completed within the specified maximum time, the Self Test Control T10 object sends a BIST test cycle overrun message to the host. See "OVERRUNTIME Field" for configuration details.

Some failures, however, cannot trigger a Message Processor T5 message, as the device is unable to function correctly (for example, a CPU or memory failure). In these cases, the firmware will reset the device and the resulting communications failure will indicate to the host that a failure has occurred.

In addition to regular BIST reporting, a GPIO pin can be configured to send a regular signals to the host to indicate that communications are working. See "TRIGGER[] Fields" for more details.

The message data for the Self Test Control T10 object is shown in Table 6-5.

TABLE 6-5: MESSAGE DATA FOR SELF TEST CONTROL T10 (SPT_SELFTESTCONTROL_T10)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>STATUS</td><td colspan="8">Result code</td></tr><tr><td>2-6</td><td>INFO</td><td colspan="8">Result data</td></tr></table>

## STATUS Field

This field contains a result code that indicates the success or failure of the test. Valid codes are given in Table 6-6.

## INFO Field

This field contains the result data of the test. The actual data depends on which test was run, as detailed below. If a test does not generate data (see Table 6-6), the INFO field consists solely of reserved bytes.

TYPE_INSTANCE Field

The instance number of the object for which a signal limit error was found.

Similarly, if a Driven Shield Signal Limits measurement fails on DS0, TYPE_NUM and TYPE_INSTANCE will indicate Self Test Signal Limits T12 Instance 0.

TABLE 6-14: SEQUENCE NUMBERS FOR PIN FAULT TEST

<table><tr><td>Code</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>0x01</td><td>Driven Ground <br> Detects shorts to a power rail</td></tr><tr><td>0x02</td><td>Driven High <br> Detects shorts to Ground</td></tr><tr><td>0x03</td><td>Walking 1 <br> Uses the pull-up resistors to detect resistive shorts</td></tr><tr><td>0x04</td><td>Walking 0 <br> Uses the pull-up resistors to detect resistive shorts</td></tr></table>

## X_PIN Field

This field indicates that a failure on an X sense pin or the GKEYX0 pin has been detected.

The value of X_PIN is 1 to 32, which represents the number of the failed X pin plus 1. For example, if X5 has failed, X_PIN will read 6. If more than one pin fails, the test reports the first failed pin detected.

Failures on the Generic Key X pin is reported following the sense pins. Thus, GKEYX0 is reported as a value of 33.

## Y_PIN Field

This field indicates that a failure on a Y sense pin or a GKEYY pin has been detected.

The value of Y_PIN is 1 to 20, which represents the number of the failed Y pin plus 1. For example, if Y3 has failed, Y_PIN will read 4. If more than one pin fails, the test reports the first failed pin detected.

Failures on the Generic Key Y pins are reported following the sense pins. Thus, GKEYY0 is reported as a value of 21, and so on.

## DS_PIN Field

This field indicates that a failure has been detected on the driven shield pin. The possible values are shown in Table 6-15.

Range: See Table 6-15

TABLE 6-15: DS_PIN VALUES

<table><tr><td>Value</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>The driven shield has passed</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>DS0 has failed</td></tr></table>

### 6.3 Self Test Pin Faults T11 Object

#### 6.3.1 INTRODUCTION

The Self Test Pin Faults T11 object specifies the configuration settings for the Pin Fault self tests. Specifically, it determines how the pin fault testing is carried out (see "PINDWELLUS Field" and "PINTHR Field").

This object is used in conjunction with the Self Test Control T10 object, which controls the tests and reports the results (see Section 6.2 "Self Test Control T10 Object").

##### 6.3.1.1 Pin Fault Tests

The Pin Fault self tests perform tests on the following pins:

- All X pins (X0 to X31)

- All Y pins (Y0 to Y19)

- All Generic Key pins (GKEYX0, and GKEYY0 to GKEYY2)

- The driven shield pin (DS0)

NOTE All the relevant pins on the device are tested, even if they have not been defined for use by any enabled touch object.

The pin fault tests allow low-resistance shorts (line-to-line, line-to-power and line-to-GND) to be detected, as well as resistive line-to-line shorts. The tests are performed by setting the pins high or low in particular sequences, as shown in Table 6-16.

TABLE 6-16: PIN FAULT TEST SEQUENCES

<table><tr><td>Sequence (Code)</td><td>Purpose</td><td>Test Operation</td></tr><tr><td>Driven Ground (0x01)</td><td>Detects shorts to a power rail (that is, they fail high). <br> Note that the detection of X/Y shorts is dependent on the supply voltage levels.</td><td>All pins are driven low to Ground.</td></tr><tr><td>Driven High (0x02)</td><td>Detects shorts to Ground (that is, they fail low). (1)</td><td>All pins are pulled high.</td></tr><tr><td>Walking 1 (0x03)</td><td>Similar to the Driven Ground sequence, but uses the pull-up resistors to detect resistive shorts. (1)</td><td>All the pins are set to zero. Then, starting with the first pin, each pin in turn is pulled high (set to 1), leaving all the other pins set to zero. The effect of this operation is that a 1 bit walks along the pins.</td></tr><tr><td>Walking 0 (0x04)</td><td>Similar to the Driven High sequence, but uses the pull-up resistors to detect resistive shorts. (1)</td><td>All the pins are set to 1. Then, starting with the first pin, each pin in turn is cleared (set to 0), leaving all the other pins set to 1 . The effect of this operation is that a "0" bit "walks" along the pins.</td></tr></table>

Note 1: Test can detect resistive shorts,but only up to \( \sim  {200}\mathrm{k}\Omega \) for the X/Y sense pins,generic key pins,and driven shield pin.

#### 6.3.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-17: CONFIGURATION FOR SELF TEST PIN FAULTS T11 (SPT_SELFTESTPINFAULT_T11)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>PINDWELLUS</td><td colspan="8">Pin dwell time</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>PINTHR</td><td colspan="8">Pin threshold</td></tr></table>

## PINDWELLUS Field

This field configures the pin dwell time (in \( \mu \mathrm{s} \) ) for the pin fault test,where 0 means use a special case of 4 * Acquisition Configuration T8 CHRGTIME (in μs). The value for this field is determined using the Microchip Sensor Design Calculator (contact your Microchip representative for more information).

If the pin fault test is enabled for POST operation (see Self Test Control T10 "POSTCFG and BISTCFG Fields"), particular care should be taken to ensure that the value of this field is set to allow enough time for the X drive lines to slew to the correct level before testing.

Range: 0 (4 x Acquisition Configuration T8 CHRGTIME), 1 to 254

## PINTHR Field

This field specifies the Pin Thresholds used to detect shorts in the pin fault tests. Increasing the value of this threshold increases the resistance that will be detected as a short.

An exact value of PINTHR can be selected using the following formula:

\[{PINTHR} = \operatorname{floor}\left( {\left( {\frac{{R}_{THR}}{{R}_{P} + {R}_{THR}} - {0.5}}\right)  \times  {512}}\right)  + 1\]

Where:

The typical value for \( {R}_{P} \) is \( {16} \times  {10}^{3} \)

The worst case value for \( {R}_{P} \) is \( {13} \times  {10}^{3} \)

\( {R}_{THR} \) is the resistance below which it is desired that a short is guaranteed to be detected.

The default value of 225 equates to a threshold of \( {200}\mathrm{k}\Omega \) ,assuming the worse case value for \( {R}_{P} \) ,and this is the recommended level. Attempting to detect short resistances larger than \( {200}\mathrm{k}\Omega \) is not recommended unless advised by Microchip.

In order to assist in tuning of this threshold, tuning data is provided by the Diagnostic Debug T37 and Command Processor T6 objects (see Section 2.2 "Diagnostic Debug T37 Object" and Section 3.3 "Command Processor T6 Object"). The tuning output provides minimum and maximum pin values detected during the last run of the pin fault test. Pin values greater than or equal to PINTHR result in a pass.

Range: 0 (225 = 200 kΩ), 1 to 255

#### 6.3.3 MESSAGES

The results of the pin fault tests are reported through the Self Test Control T10 object. See Section 6.2.3 "Messages" for details.

#### 6.3.4 DIAGNOSTIC DEBUG DATA

The diagnostic debug data modes for the Self Test Pin Faults T11 object is shown in Table 6-18. The diagnostic debug data can be viewed in the Diagnostic Debug T37 object by using the appropriate Command Processor T6 command, also listed in Table 6-18.

The diagnostic debug modes are described in the following sections.

TABLE 6-18: DIAGNOSTIC DEBUG COMMANDS

<table><tr><td>T6 Command</td><td>Name</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>0x35</td><td>Pin Fault Self Test Mode</td><td>The Diagnostic Debug T37 object holds the tuning data for the Self Test Control T10 pin fault tests. See Section 6.3.4.1 "Pin Fault Self Test Mode".</td></tr></table>

6.3.4.1 Pin Fault Self Test Mode

Figure 6-2 shows the format of the data in Pin Fault Self Test Mode. This reports the tuning data reported by the Self Test Control T10 object for the pin fault test.

<table><tr><td>Page</td><td>Data Index Data[]</td><td></td></tr><tr><td rowspan="5">Page 0</td><td></td><td>0 Minimum measured pin value for a pin that is expected to be pulled low</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>1 Maximum measured pin value for a pin that is expected to be pulled low</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>2 Minimum measured pin value for a pin that is expected to be pulled high</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>3 Maximum measured pin value for a pin that is expected to be pulled high</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>4-127 Reserved</td></tr></table>

### 6.4 Self Test Signal Limits T12 Object

#### 6.4.1 INTRODUCTION

The Self Test Signal Limits T12 object specifies the configuration settings for the Signal Limit self tests. Specifically, it determines how the signal limit testing is carried out.

The Signal limit tests test the signals from the touch object associated with this instance of the Self Test Signal Limits T12 object. The user must specify the expected minimum and maximum level for the associated touch object under test, using the SIGLIMUP, SIGLIMLO and SIGLIMRANGE fields.

This object is used in conjunction with the Self Test Control T10 object, which controls the tests and reports the results (see Section 6.2 "Self Test Control T10 Object"). Note that Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 must be enabled for the tests to run successfully.

On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family there are 2 instances of the Self Test Signal Limits T12 object, one for each touch object on the device. Note that the Signal Limit self tests are run for each enabled touch object rather than for the entire touchscreen sensor matrix.

TABLE 6-19: SELF TEST SIGNAL LIMITS T12 INSTANCES

<table><tr><td>Instance</td><td>Purpose</td></tr><tr><td>Instance 0</td><td>Configures Signal Limit self tests for Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100. <br> This instance also configures the Driven Shield Signal Limit tests for DS0.</td></tr><tr><td>Instance 1</td><td>Configures Signal Limit self tests for Key Array T15.</td></tr></table>

NOTE For free-form (non rectangular) screens, it is possible to use the Ignore Nodes T141 and Ignore Nodes Controller T145 objects to indicate that certain nodes are to be ignored by the Signal Limit self tests. See Section 5.16 "Ignore Nodes T141 Object" and Section 6.22 "Ignore Nodes Controller T145 Object" for more details.

##### 6.4.1.1 Signal Limit Tests

For a Self Test Signal Limits T12 instance that tests the signal limits, the SIGLIMLO and SIGLIMUP fields specify the lower and upper signal limits for the signal limit tests. When the test is run, the mutual capacitance signals must fall between SIGLIMLO and SIGLIMUP for the test to pass. Any signal values outside this range will generate a signal limit error in the test.

The SIGLIMRANGE field specifies the signal range limit used by the signal limit tests for the associated touch object under test. When the test is run, the difference between the largest and smallest mutual capacitance signal must be less than the value specified in SIGLIMRANGE for the test to pass.

For a touchscreen operating with P2P Mutual Capacitance measurements enabled (see Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 "CALCFG Field"), it is necessary to specify separate single-ended mutual capacitance measurement gains for the Signal Limit tests. See "GAIN Field" and "DXGAIN Field" for more details.

NOTE The Self Test Signal Limits T12 object should have an appropriate configuration for signal limit tests, especially the gains for signal limit testing, in order to avoid other self test failures occurring even if signal limit testing is not enabled.

6.4.1.2 Driven Shield Signal Limits Test

If the Driven Shield Signal Limits test is enabled (see "CTRL Field"), the Signal Limit tests also test the signal limits on the DS0 pin. This allows open circuit faults on the DS0 pin to be detected. The DSGAIN field must be set for this test to operate correctly (see "DSGAIN Field").

Note that Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 CTRL DISMEASX must also be set to 0 if the Driven Shield Signal Limits test is enabled.

#### 6.4.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-20: CONFIGURATION FOR SELF TEST SIGNAL LIMITS T12 - MULTIPLE TOUCH TOUCHSCREEN T100 INSTANCES (SPT_SELFTESTSIGLIMIT_T12)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td>DSTESTEN</td><td colspan="7">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>GAIN</td><td colspan="8">Gain</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>DXGAIN</td><td colspan="8">Dual X gain</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td rowspan="2">SIGLIMLO</td><td colspan="8">Signal lower limit LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td colspan="8">Signal lower limit MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td rowspan="2">SIGLIMUP</td><td colspan="8">Signal upper limit LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td colspan="8">Signal upper limit MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td rowspan="2">SIGLIMRANGE</td><td colspan="8">Signal range limit LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td colspan="8">Signal range limit MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>DSGAIN</td><td colspan="8">Driven shield gain</td></tr></table>

TABLE 6-21: CONFIGURATION FOR SELF TEST SIGNAL LIMITS T12 - KEY ARRAY T15 INSTANCES (SPT_SELFTESTSIGLIMIT_T12)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td rowspan="2">SIGLIMLO</td><td colspan="8">Signal lower limit LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td colspan="8">Signal lower limit MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td rowspan="2">SIGLIMUP</td><td colspan="8">Signal upper limit LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td colspan="8">Signal upper limit MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td rowspan="2">SIGLIMRANGE</td><td colspan="8">Signal range limit LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td colspan="8">Signal range limit MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr></table>

CTRL Field

DSTESTEN: Enables the inclusion of the Driven Shield Signal Limits tests for DS0, as part of the standard Signal Limit tests. This control is set to 1 to enable the Driven Shield Signal Limits tests, and set to 0 to disable the tests.

NOTE

- The Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 object must be enabled for use, and Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 CTRL DISMEASX must be set to 0 (that is, the X axis measurement must not be disabled), for the Driven Shield Signal Limit tests to operate.

- If the Driven Shield Signal Limits Test is enabled for use (DSTESTEN = 1), low frequency compensation cannot be used and must therefore be disabled by setting Self Capacitance Configuration T111 CTRL LFCOMPEN to 0 (see Self Capacitance Configuration T111 "CTRL Field").

NOTE This control is present on Self Test Signal Limits T12 Instance 0 only, and operates on DS0.

## GAIN Field

NOTE This field is used by Self Test Signal Limits T12 Instance 0 only (that is, the instance linked to Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100): this field is not used by the Self Test Signal Limits T12 instance linked to Key Array T15.

This field specifies the Single-ended Mutual Capacitance Measurement Gain for the Signal Limit tests. If P2P Mutual Capacitance measurements are enabled (see Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 "CALCFG Field"), the Signal Limit tests require the running of additional Single-ended Mutual Capacitance measurements. These measurements will use a different gain setting when running in Single X mode to that of the normal Mutual Capacitance measurements (which use the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 Single X gain setting). This field specifies this additional Single X gain setting.

If P2P Mutual Capacitance measurements are not enabled (Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 CALCFG P2PMUTUALEN = 0), this field should be set to the same value as Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 GAIN.

Range: 0 to 22

## DXGAIN Field

NOTE This field is used by Self Test Signal Limits T12 Instance 0 only (that is, the instance linked to Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100): this field is not used by the Self Test Signal Limits T12 instance linked to Key Array T15.

This field specifies the Single-ended Dual X Mutual Capacitance Measurement Gain for the Signal Limit Test. If P2P Mutual Capacitance measurements are enabled (see Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 "CALCFG Field"), the Signal Limit Tests require the running of additional Single-ended Mutual Capacitance measurements. These measurements will use a different gain setting when running in Dual X mode to that of the normal Mutual Capacitance measurements (which use the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 Dual X gain setting). This field specifies this additional Dual X gain setting.

If P2P Mutual Capacitance measurements are not enabled (Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 CALCFG P2PMUTUALEN = 0), this field should be set to the same value as Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 DXGAIN.

A value of 255 in the field turns on auto correction of the gain in Dual X mode. In Dual X two X lines are pulsed at the same time so there will be double the amount of charge present. The purpose of the auto correction is to halve the system gain so it is at the correct level.

Range: 0 to 22, 255 (auto correction)

## SIGLIMLO and SIGLIMUP Fields

These fields specify the signal limits used by the signal limit tests for the touch object associated with this instance of the Self Test Signal Limits T12 object (see Section 6.4.1.1 "Signal Limit Tests").

The values of SIGLIMLO and SIGLIMUP should be chosen depending on whether the unit is a design prototype or a production item.

For production use, SIGLIMLO should never be lower than 1200 and SIGLIMUP should never be higher than 14600. The exact values, however, are determined by analyzing the data from actual sensor samples. Using the full range can cause sensors that have too much signal to pass the test.

Range: See Table 6-22

TABLE 6-22: RECOMMENDED VALUES FOR SIGLIMLO[] AND SIGLIMUP[]

<table><tr><td rowspan="2">Touch Object</td><td colspan="2">Limits</td><td colspan="2">Recommended Design Values</td><td colspan="2">Recommended Production Values</td></tr><tr><td>SIGLIMLO</td><td>SIGLIMUP</td><td>SIGLIMLO</td><td>SIGLIMUP</td><td>SIGLIMLO</td><td>SIGLIMUP</td></tr><tr><td>Key Array T15</td><td>1200</td><td>14600</td><td>6800</td><td>10200</td><td colspan="2">Determined on a case-by-case basis</td></tr><tr><td>Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100</td><td>1200</td><td>14600</td><td>6800</td><td>10200</td><td colspan="2">Determined on a case-by-case basis</td></tr></table>

Note: SIGLIMUP must be \( \geq \) SIGLIMLO

## SIGLIMRANGE Field

This field specifies the signal range limit used by the signal limit tests for the touch object associated with this instance of the Self Test Signal Limits T12 object (see Section 6.4.1.1 "Signal Limit Tests").

Range: 1 to 13500

## DSGAIN Field

NOTE This field is present on Self Test Signal Limits T12 Instance 0 only, and operates on DS0.

This field configures the Gain for the Driven Shield Signal Limits test measurements for DS0.

Range: 0 to 29, 128 to 157 (Gain × 2 mode)

This field must be tuned such that the driven shield signal limit value remains saturated throughout normal operation. See Figure 2-5 on page 18 for details on how to read the value. Note that when the signal goes above the saturation level (that is, above a value of -16384), the Self Test Control T10 object reports a DS signal limit failure (that is, a Signal Limit Error with a TYPE_INSTANCE of 12; see "DATA Field - Signal Limit Error" on page 188).

#### 6.4.3 MESSAGES

The results of the signal limit tests are reported through the Self Test Control T10 object. See Section 6.2.3 "Messages" for details.

## mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family 1.0

ReportID[13]</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables this instance of the Communications Configuration T18 object. Enabling Instance 1 effectively enables a secondary communications interface and associates it with this Communications Configuration T18 instance

NOTE This control is applicable to Instance 1 only: Instance 0 (that is, the primary communications interface) is always enabled (and cannot be disabled).

This control must be set at reset time to take effect.

MODE: Selects the CHG_I2C line mode for \( {I}^{2}\mathrm{C} \) communications over the \( {I}^{2}\mathrm{C} \) interface. If this bit is set to 0 (the default), the CHG_I2C line operates in Mode 0. If this bit is set to 1, the CHG_I2C line operates in Mode 1. Refer to the relevant device Datasheet for more information on the modes for the CHG_I2C line.

NOTE This control has an effect only on an instance of Communications Configuration T18 used to define \( {I}^{2}C \) communications; it has no effect on an instance of Communications Configuration T18 used to define SPI communications.

RETRIGEN: Enables CHG I2C or CHG SPI line host retriggering mode. This provides extra edge-based interrupts to the host on the CHG_I2C or CHG_SPI line (as appropriate for this instance). This mode is enabled if this bit is set to 1 and disabled if set to 0 . If this mode is enabled, the CHG_I2C or CHG_SPI line is deasserted once every acquisition cycle for \( {50}\mathrm{{\mu s}} \) and then re-asserted. This creates edges on the CHG_I2C or CHG_SPI line for the host in case it missed the CHG_I2C or CHG_SPI line being asserted.

This re-triggering mechanism is performed once every acquisition cycle, if the time elapsed since the last time the CHG_I2C line was asserted is greater than 10 ms (if the \( {l}^{2}C \) interface is used for host communications),or if the time elapsed since the last time the CHG_SPI line was asserted is greater than 3 ms (if the SPI interface is used for host communications). This means that, if the configured acquisition interval is less than 10 ms or 3 ms (as appropriate), one or more extra acquisition cycles will be necessary to lapse for the CHG_I2C or CHG_SPI line to be re-triggered, as determined by Power Configuration T7 IDLEACQINT and ACTVACQINT (see "IDLEACQINT and ACTVACQINT Fields").

Note that if the \( {I}^{2}C \) interface is used,and command code 2 or 3 is set in the COMMAND field,then the command will override the RETRIGEN mode setting.

## COMMAND Field

The COMMAND field provides direct control over the CHG_I2C line for the \( {I}^{2}C \) interface. This overrides the operation of the CHG_I2C line controlled by the MODE bit in the CTRL field. Entering one of the command codes listed in Table 6-26 alters the state of the CHG_I2C line.

NOTE This control has an effect only if the \( {I}^{2}C \) interface is used for host communications; it has no effect if the SPI interface is used for host communications.

TABLE 6-26: COMMAND CODES

<table><tr><td>Command</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>No command (default)</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Return the CHG_I2C line to normal operation, as determined by the MODE bit of the CTRL field</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>Force the CHG_I2C line high (inactive)</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>Force the CHG_I2C line low (active)</td></tr></table>

## CFG Field

COMMSTYPE: On Instance 1, specifies the communications interface type to be associated with this instance. In other words, it specifies which secondary communications interface is to be used.

NOTE This control is applicable to Instance 1 only. The communications interface type for instance 0 is preset by the hardware.

This control must be set at reset time to take effect.

COMMSTYPE Range: See Table 6-27

## TABLE 6-27: COMMSTYPE

<table><tr><td>Command</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Use the SPI Interface as the secondary communications interface</td></tr><tr><td>2 to 15</td><td>Reserved</td></tr></table>

## DISRPTMASK[] Fields

These fields form an array of bitmaps that indicate which report IDs are to be ignored (disabled) when outputting messages, thus allowing for different reporting behavior on both interfaces.

By default if an object that generates messages has its CTRL RPTEN bit set, it will output messages for all report IDs over all active interfaces. These fields allow reporting to be disabled for the interface associated with this instance on a report ID basis (thus vetoing the object's CTRL RPTEN bit).

NOTE The appropriate object's CTRL RPTEN bit must be set in order for a message to be sent for a particular report ID: if an object's CTRL RPTEN is set to 0 (disabled), then a message will never be sent, even if the appropriate bit in the DISRPTMASK is set to 0 (enabled).

See Section 1.5.6 "Report IDs" for more information on report IDs.

### 6.6 GPIO Configuration T19 Object

#### 6.6.1 INTRODUCTION

The GPIO Configuration T19 object sets up the general-purpose I/O pins. The pins can be set as input or output pins.

Note that the reporting of signals on the input pins occurs only at the appropriate point in the acquisition cycle. This means that the input signal must not occur faster than the Idle or Active Acquisition Interval specified in the Power Configuration T7 object (see Section 3.4 "Power Configuration T7 Object"). Similar criteria apply if an output bit is changed. This operation does not take place instantaneously and enough time must be allowed for it to happen.

IMPORTANT! If the GPIO pins are used on a UL/IEC 60730 Class B compliant product, it is the responsibility of the host system design to ensure that GPIO Configuration T19 GPIO functionality meets UL/IEC 60730 Class B requirements. This applies in particular to the use of GPIO output pins.

- The GPIO0 function shares a pin with the SYNC function. If the SYNC function is enabled, then this takes precedence over any specified GPIO0 function.

- The hardware debug functionality is shared with some of the GPIO pins. If the hardware debug interface is in use, then these pins cannot be used as GPIO pins. Refer to the relevant device Datasheet for details on the hardware debug interface.

The GPIO pins can be used to trigger events, either by transitions from high to low, or vice versa, during use, or by setting the pin high at startup. Note that for the event to be generated, the GPIO pin needs to be set as an output and not overridden by an alternative function.

#### 6.6.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-28: CONFIGURATION FOR GPIO CONFIGURATION T19 (SPT_GPIOPWM_T19)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td colspan="5">Reserved</td><td>FORCERPT</td><td>RPTEN</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>REPORTMASK (1)</td><td colspan="8">Report mask bit field</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>DIR (1)</td><td colspan="8">Pin direction bit field</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>INTPULLUP (1)</td><td colspan="8">Internal pull-ups bit field</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>OUT (1)</td><td colspan="8">Output value bit field</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>WAKE (2)</td><td colspan="8">Wake up on bit change bit field</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td>TRIGGER[0]</td><td colspan="8">Trigger for GPIOO</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>14</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>15</td><td>Reserved</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td>Reserved</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables or disables the use of the GPIO Configuration T19 object. The object is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0 .

RPTEN: Enables or disables the GPIO Configuration T19 object to report messages. If this bit is set, the device sends messages on bit changes. Reporting is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0.

FORCERPT: Writing a 1 to this bit forces the GPIO Configuration T19 object to send a message with its current status. The object then clears this bit. The RPTEN bit must be enabled for this to work. See Section 6.6.3 "Messages" for information on the message data.

## REPORTMASK Field

Specifies a bit mask that suppresses the sending of messages on bit changes. Set these bits to 1 if the corresponding GPIO pins should not generate a message on a bit change. The pins must be set as input pins in the DIR field. The default value of 0 causes all bit changes to generate messages.

## DIR Field

Sets the direction of the pins: \( 1 = \operatorname{GPIO}n \) is an output pin; \( 0 = \operatorname{GPIO}n \) is an input pin.

The default value of 0 sets a pin as an input pin, in which case if the pin is unused, it should be connected as described in the relevant device Datasheet.

NOTE If the pins are set as inputs (or are left in their default state) and the object is subsequently enabled, the input pins are assumed to have a low initial state.

## INTPULLUP Field

Enables the internal pull-up resistors for any input pins. If these bits are set to 1, the internal pull-up resistors for the corresponding pins are enabled. The pins must be set as input pins in the DIR field. If this field is set to 0 (default), all the internal pull-up resistors for the pins are disabled.

## OUT Field

Sets the state of the output GPIO pins. Setting these bits to 1 sets the pins high. Clearing these bits to 0 sets the pins low. The pins must already be set as output pins in the DIR field.

## WAKE Field

NOTE On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family, the wake feature is not supported for GPIO1 or GPIO2.

Causes the device to wake up on bit changes if it is asleep. If these bits are set to 1, the device will wake up on a bit change on the IO pins. When the bit change occurs, the device wakes up, reports the GPIO message and then returns to sleep. The pins must already be set as input pins in the DIR field. If this field is set to 0 (default), the device will remain asleep on bit changes.

## TRIGGER[] Fields

NOTE On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family, trigger functionality can be enabled on GPIO0 only.

These fields select a trigger source for the corresponding GPIO pin (see Table 6-31 and Table 6-32). The trigger inverts the appropriate GPIO pin if the source object is active. The pin must be set as an output pin in the DIR field.

Note that on entering Deep Sleep mode, any triggered pins stick at their current triggered state until the device wakes again.

TABLE 6-31: TRIGGER GPIO PINS

<table><tr><td>Field</td><td>GPIO Pin</td></tr><tr><td>TRIGGER[0]</td><td>Selects a trigger source for GPIO0 pin</td></tr></table>

Range: See Table 6-32

TABLE 6-32: TRIGGER[] FIELD VALUES

<table><tr><td>Value</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>0 (or not listed below)</td><td>Trigger disabled.</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Triggered whenever any touch is detected on Key 0 of the Key Array T15 object. Note that the trigger is related to the actual key and is not affected by any Key IDs configured by the Key ID Configuration T16 object.</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>Triggered whenever the Self Test Control T10 object sends an All BIST Tests Passed message (see Section 6.2.1.2 "Built-In Self Test (BIST)"). This can be used to provide a heartbeat ("alive") signal for functional safety purposes.</td></tr></table>

STATUS: Gives the current state of all GPIO pins that are set as inputs. Any GPIO pin that is set as an output reports as a zero. This field is a bit field with each bit representing a GPIO pin. See Table 6-29 on page 201 for the format of this field.

### 6.7 User Data T38 Object

#### 6.7.1 INTRODUCTION

The User Data T38 object provides a small area on the device for the user to store their own custom data, such as the user's own version information. The size of this area varies from device to device. On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family the size of this area is 64 bytes.

Any data stored in this object will be backed up to the non-volatile memory when the Command Processor T6 object processes a backup command (see Section 3.3 "Command Processor T6 Object").

NOTE The data is not included in the checksum reported by the Command Processor T6 after a backup has been processed.

#### 6.7.2 CONFIGURATION

## TABLE 6-34: CONFIGURATION FOR SPT_USERDATA_T38

## DATA[] Field

This field contains the user's data.

NOTE The User Data T38 object does not provide any mechanism for checking the integrity of the data held within the object. It is therefore the responsibility of the host to perform any such checks for compliance with UL/IEC 60730 Class B.

### 6.8 CTE Configuration T46 Object

#### 6.8.1 INTRODUCTION

The CTE Configuration T46 object controls how the capacitive touch engine (CTE) in the device samples the mutual capacitive signals. This object also controls pulse synchronization during mutual capacitance measurements.

The X (drive) lines are sampled one at a time, with at least 2 analog-to-digital conversions (ADCs) performed on each X line in turn. The number of ADCs per X line is configured by a combination of the ACTVSYNCSPERX / IDLESYNCSPERX and ADCSPERSYNC fields.

The number of ADCs per X is a nominal value only. Other objects can suggest other values for the ADCs per X setting under specific circumstances, such as when external noise is detected or when a stylus is in use. The mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family will use the highest required setting for ADCs per X, as determined by the various objects. The objects that can suggest a maximum ADCs per X settings include:

- Passive Stylus T47 for use with passive stylus touches

- Glove Detection T78 for use with glove touches

- Noise Suppression T72 for use when external noise has been detected

NOTE The minimum Active/Idle ADCs per X is saturated to 2. Therefore, if less than 2 ADCs per X is configured, 2 ADCs per X will be used.

The number of pulses for each ADC can also be configured. The amount of signal measured depends on the number of pulses per ADC. The more pulses per ADC, the higher the amount of charge that is measured. The number of pulses per ADC is determined by the PULSESPERADC field (see "PULSESPERADC Field").

Therefore,if ADCSPERSYNC = 0 or 1, the total number of pulses per X line is equivalent to:

(PULSESPERADC+1) \( \times \) (ACTVSYNCSPERX or IDLESYNCSPERX)

Alternatively,if ADCSPERSYNC \( \geq  2 \) ,the total number of pulses per X line is equivalent to:

(PULSESPERADC+1) \( \times \) (ADCSPERSYNC-1) \( \times \) (ACTVSYNCSPERX or IDLESYNCSPERX)

6.8.1.1 Pulse Synchronization

IMPORTANT! Pulse Synchronization functionality on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family is not considered UL/IEC 60730 Class B compliant. Therefore, the device should not be configured to use Pulse Synchronization in a UL/IEC 60730 Class B product.

NOTE The SYNC line can be used for either pulse synchronization or frame synchronization (see "SYNC Field"), but not both. If the SYNC line is used for pulse synchronization functionality, then it cannot be used for frame synchronization.

The ADCSPERSYNC field determines how the ADCs are synchronized to the SYNC line, if at all:

- If the ADCSPERSYNC field is set to zero, then no pulse synchronization occurs for mutual capacitance measurements.

- If the ADCSPERSYNC field is set to 1, then pulse synchronization occurs for mutual capacitance measurements. In this case, the rising and falling X edges of each ADC are synchronized to the falling edge of the SYNC signal.

- If the ADCSPERSYNC field is set to a value of 2 or above, the ADCs are arranged in "Sync Groups". The number of ADCs per Sync Group is (ADCSPERSYNC - 1). In this case, the ACTVSYNCSPERX and IDLESYNCSPERX fields determine the number of Sync Groups per X line. Thus, the total number of ADCs per X is equivalent to: (ADCSPERSYNC - 1) * ACTVSYNCSPERX or IDLESYNCSPERX

with a minimum value of 2 .

Note the following:

- Pulse synchronization is enabled for each measurement type independently. To enable pulse synchronization on self capacitance measurement types, see Section 6.16 "Self Capacitance Configuration T111 Object"

- If pulse synchronization is turned on (that is, ADCSPERSYNC is non-zero), GPIO0 cannot be configured by the GPIO Configuration T19 object. GPIO0 should be set as an input, or the GPIO Configuration T19 object disabled, for the pulse synchronization to work.

If there is a requirement to toggle pulse synchronization on and off at run time, the device must be configured and backed up with pulse synchronization enabled in either CTE Configuration T46 or Self Capacitance Configuration T111. This ensures that the device will start up with pulse synchronization enabled for at least one measurement type and the SYNC pin is latched for use. This prevents the pin from being used for other uses, such as configured as GPIO0 by the GPIO Configuration T19 object.

CTE CONFIGURATION T46 PULSE SYNCHRONIZATION

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_205.jpg?x=197&y=458&w=1409&h=979&r=0"/>

If the system has been configured to use pulse synchronization and there is a failure to detect a SYNC signal, the default behavior of the system is to continue measurements unsynchronized using user-configured timing. If this behavior is not required, CFG SYNCLOSSMODE can be set to 1 to pause measurements altogether while pulse synchronization is absent. When a SYNC signal is subsequently detected, pulse synchronization will be re-enabled and the measurements will continue with synchronized ADCs. Note that CTE Configuration T46 CFG SYNCLOSSMODE has an effect on all mutual and self capacitance measurements.

6.8.2 SPREAD SPECTRUM

NOTE Use of Spread Spectrum Variance is incompatible with Pulse Synchronization functionality. If Pulse Synchronization functionality is enabled at the same time as SPREADSPECVAR (see "ADCSPERSYNC Field"), then Pulse Synchronization will take precedence.

The X drive burst pulses can have a spread spectrum algorithm applied that applies a decreasing frequency (spread spectrum variance) to the bursts (see "SPREADSPECVAR Field"). The Spread Spectrum algorithm calculates a set of 16 decreasing frequencies, starting with the base frequency (that is, frequency 1 is equal to the base frequency), and these 16 frequencies are then applied to the X drive burst pulses in the following order:

Frequency 1 ... Frequency \( n \)

where \( n \) is the number of pulses.

If the number of pulses per X line is less than 16, then not all 16 frequencies will be used and the effective spread spectrum variance is reduced.

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_206.jpg?x=137&y=300&w=1428&h=721&r=0"/>

Fn = Calculated frequency number

## IDLESYNCSPERX Field

This field sets the number of ADCs per X in Idle mode. The range for this field is 1 to 255, where a value of 0 means 8.

See Section 6.8.1 "Introduction" for more information on how this field helps determine the actual number of ADCs per X.

Range: 0 (8), 1 to 255

## ACTVSYNCSPERX Field

This field determines the number of ADCs per X in Active mode. The range for this field is 1 to 255, where a value of 0 means 8 .

See Section 6.8.1 "Introduction" for more information on how this field helps determine the actual number of ADCs per X.

Range: 0 (8), 1 to 255

## ADCSPERSYNC Field

NOTE If synchronization is turned on (that is, ADCSPERSYNC is non-zero), GPIO0 cannot be configured by the GPIO Configuration T19 object. GPIO0 must be set as an input, or the GPIO Configuration T19 object disabled, for the CTE Configuration T46 burst pulse synchronization to work.

ADCSPERSYNC: Determines whether or not the ADC conversions are synchronized to the SYNC pin for mutual capacitance measurements. To enable pulse synchronization on self capacitance measurement types, see Section 6.16 "Self Capacitance Configuration T111 Object".

A value of 0 means no synchronization is required (that is, mutual capacitance measurements are not synchronized to the input signal on the SYNC pin).

A value of 1 synchronizes the rising and falling X edges of each ADC to the falling edge of the SYNC signal (see Figure 6-3 on page 206 for an example).

A value equal to or greater than 2 determines the number (value minus 1) of ADCs per Sync Group.

Range: 0 (no synchronization),

1 (ADCs synchronized to SYNC)

2 to 63

## PULSESPERADC Field

This field determines the number of pulses for each ADC conversion. This is specified as the number of pulses minus 1. The range for this field is 0 to 3 , which represents 1 to 4 pulses.

Range: 0 to 3

## XSLEW Field

This field sets the X slew rate. The valid values for this field are given in Table 6-36.

## TABLE 6-36: XSLEW SETTINGS

SYNCDELAY Field

This 16-bit field specifies the delay from when the SYNC falling edge occurs to when the X edge is generated. The delay is specified in units of the CTE clock period (20 ns; 50 MHz), where a value of 0 means no delay.

Range: 0 (no delay), 1 to 65534

## XVOLTAGE Field

This field specifies the voltage for XVdd. Refer to the relevant device Datasheet for information on configuring the hardware to operate correctly at the selected XVdd voltage level.

NOTE The device should be backed up and reset for this setting to take effect.

CFG Field

NOTE The CFG field control applies to all mutual and self capacitance measurement types in the device.

DISTEMPCOMP: Disables Temperature Compensation. When this control is set to 1, temperature compensation for both mutual capacitance and self capacitance measurements is disabled. It is not recommended to set this control to 1 unless advised to do so by Microchip.

Note that temperature compensation is also disabled when pulse synchronization is active but SYNCPERIOD is 0 (see "SYNCPERIOD Field").

SYNCLOSSMODE: Specifies the Synchronization Loss Mode. This controls the system behavior when the SYNC pulse is lost for pulse synchronized measurements.

If this bit is set to 0, all measurements will continue to measure in an unsynchronized manner with timing based upon configuration settings.

If this bit is set to 1, mutual and self capacitance measurements will cease to measure until the pulse synchronization signal returns.

DELTASHIFT: Specifies the Delta Shift that is used to scale (shift right) all 8-bit and 16-bit deltas, except single-ended self capacitance deltas, in any debug data. The delta scaling also allows for thresholds to be specified as 8-bit values for configuration purposes. See Section 1.9.1 "Delta Scaling" for details.

By default (DELTASHIFT = 0) no shift occurs (that is, there is no scaling applied), although the device still converts between 8-bit and 16-bit deltas where necessary. By setting this control to a value greater than 0, a greater usable range for all 8-bit threshold controls can be used.

IMPORTANT! Modifying the delta scaling may affect the configuration values used for various threshold and gain values. The device may therefore need retuning if DELTASHIFT is altered.

Range: See Table 6-40

TABLE 6-40: DELTASHIFT CONTROL

<table><tr><td>DELTASHIFT Value</td><td>Scaling</td><td>Maximum Thresholdable Unscaled 16-bit Delta</td></tr><tr><td>0 (default)</td><td>\( \div  1 \)</td><td>2040</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>\( \div  2 \)</td><td>4080</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>\( \div  4 \)</td><td>8160</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>\( \div  8 \)</td><td>16320</td></tr></table>

## SYNCPERIOD Field

NOTE The SYNCPERIOD field control applies to all mutual and self capacitance measurement types in the device that use the Pulse Synchronization functionality.

This control sets the nominal SYNC clock period. This setting is required for both mutual capacitance and self capacitance touch temperature compensation if the pulse synchronization feature is enabled (see "ADCSPERSYNC Field").

The period is specified in units of the CTE clock period (20 ns; 50 MHz), where a value of 0 is not recommended unless advised by Microchip.

Range: 0 to 65535

## SPREADSPECVAR Field

NOTE Use of Spread Spectrum Variance is incompatible with Pulse Synchronization functionality. If Pulse Synchronization functionality is enabled at the same time as SPREADSPECVAR (see "ADCSPERSYNC Field"), then Pulse Synchronization will take precedence.

This field specifies the Spread Spectrum Variance. This is the overall total percentage variance when applying spread spectrum to mutual capacitance measurements and determines the amount the frequency decreases over each set of bursts (see Section 6.8.2 "Spread Spectrum").

The Spread Spectrum Variance is specified as a sliding range from 0 to 127, which represents a range of 0 to 20% percent frequency decrease (which corresponds to a 25% increase in the period). The default value of 0 means that spread spectrum functionality is disabled.

Range: 0 (disabled), 1 to 127

## YPHASEDELAY Field

This field specifies the Y Line Phase Delay. This is the delay between each Y line setup (biasing) before measurement. This field applies to all mutual and self capacitance measurements.

The delay is specified in units of the CTE clock period (20 ns; 50 MHz).

NOTE The transition from a mutual capacitance measurement to a self capacitance measurement does not use Y line phasing if self capacitance pre-charge is disabled (see Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 "CTRL Field" DISPRECHARGE control). In this case, settings configured for Voltage Modulation are used instead (see Section 6.20 "Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 Object").

Note that the phase delay is still present at this transition, as X lines are also phased at this point.

Range: 0 to 65535

#### 6.8.4 CONFIGURATION CHECKS

The CTE Configuration T46 object causes a configuration check to be performed in the following circumstances:

- When certain fields are changed

A configuration check may determine that a configuration error has occurred (for example, if a setting is set outside of its allowed range or a conflict has occurred between two settings). This is signaled to the host (see Section 3.3.3 "Messages"), and the device halts until the error has been corrected. To fix the error, the object settings should be checked to verify that they are all within their allowed limits, as stated in the field descriptions.

## STATUS Field

CHKERR: Not used in this product; this field should always report a zero value.

### 6.9 Timer T61 Object

#### 6.9.1 INTRODUCTION

The Timer T61 object provides a timer that can be set up to trigger either a single message after a delay or a stream of regular messages. When the timer expires, a message is sent in the appropriate manner. The timer has two modes, set by the MODE field:

- Single trigger mode: Triggers a single message after a specified period.

- Repeat trigger mode: Triggers repeat messages at a specified interval.

There are 6 instances of the Timer T61 object on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family.

#### 6.9.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-43: CONFIGURATION FOR TIMER T61

(SPT_TIMER_T61)

CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables or disables the use of the Timer T61 object. The object is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0 .

RPTEN: Enables or disables the Timer T61 object to report messages. Reporting is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0 .

This field is cleared to zero once the command has been processed. Note that the host should write a command to this field only if the field is zero (that is, the previous command has been processed), otherwise the previous command will be overwritten.

## MODE Field

MODE: Configures the timer mode; see Table 6-45.

STATUS Field

CNTVAL Field

This field reports the current timer count value.

### 6.10 Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 Object

#### 6.10.1 INTRODUCTION

A Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object provides a flexible way for the host to change configurations during runtime in response to a trigger. The configurations are defined for a specific event and when that event is triggered, the associated configuration settings are changed. There are 20 instances of the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family.

Events can take two forms:

- Double edge event

A double edge event is an event with an on and off state (such as a touch) and can therefore be considered to have a rising edge and a falling edge. The rising edge is the positive state change at the start of the event and the falling edge is the negative state change at the end of the event.

For example, a noise detection event typically has two edges: the first (rising) edge is a change from a "no noise" to a "noise detected" state, and the second (falling) edge is the change back from a "noise detected" to a "no noise" state.

Host defined events have the behavior of double edge events.

- Single edge event

A single edge event is an event with a positive state change only.

For example, a calibration command is a single edge event.

A Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object can be configured to respond to the following:

- A single edge event

- A single edge (rising or falling) of a double edge event

- Both edges of a double edge event

The ENUMID of the EVENT field is used to specify which event to trigger on.

Alternative sets of configuration settings can be read from either the Non-volatile memory (NVM) or from the Dynamic Configuration Container T71 object (see Section 6.11 "Dynamic Configuration Container T71 Object"), as selected by the ALTSRC bit of the CTRL field. If the settings are to be read from the Dynamic Configuration Container T71 object, the SRCOFFSET field specifies the offset to use.

Note that, in the case of the Command Processor T6, the bytes that contain the RESET and BACKUPNV fields cannot be loaded with configuration data. That is, If the OBJTYPE is 6 (Command Processor T6), then DSTOFFSET must be at least 2 with an appropriate LENGTH, otherwise a configuration error is generated. All other objects in the device, including the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 itself, can be loaded with new configuration data.

The BACKUPNV Field of the Command Processor T6 object supports commands that help avoid the issue of a Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object modifying settings before they are backed up. The host can also restore a configuration from the NVM using the Command Processor T6 object. The restore function does not require a reset. See Section 3.3 "Command Processor T6 Object" for more details.

To set up and use a Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object:

1. Stop the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object using the BACKUPNV field in the Command Processor T6 object (See Section 3.3.2 "Configuration").

2. Write the intended settings to the device and back up the configuration to NVM.

Figure 6-5 shows an example of using a Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object to set up a double edge trigger for a host event (EVENT HOSTDEF = 1) that loads alternative Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 settings.

In this case, CTRL ALTSRC is set to 0 so that the configuration data is read from the Dynamic Configuration Container T71 object on the rising edge (event start) and from NVM on the falling edge (event end). The configuration data consists of 25 bytes of the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 settings, starting from byte 28 (GAIN).

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_215.jpg?x=299&y=242&w=1259&h=817&r=0"/>

E 6-5: EXAMPLE HOST EVENT - LOADING ALTERNATIVE MULTIPLE TOUCH

Figure 6-6 shows an example of using two separate Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object instances to set up two triggers for noise events: one on the rising edge (EVENT ENUMID = 24) on the transition from the STABLE to NOISY state, and one on the falling edge (EVENT ENUMID = 21) on the transition from the NOISY to STABLE state.

5-6: EXAMPLE SINGLE EDGE EVENTS – LOADING MULTIPLE TOUCH TOUCHSCREEN T100 SETTINGS IN RESPONSE TO NOISE

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_215.jpg?x=350&y=1304&w=1219&h=793&r=0"/>

In this case, alternative settings are loaded for Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 at the start of the noise event and NVM settings reloaded at the end of the noise event. As with Figure 6-5, the configuration data consists of 25 bytes of the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 settings, starting from byte 28 (GAIN).

TABLE 6-47: CONFIGURATION FOR DYNAMIC CONFIGURATION CONTROLLER T70 (SPT_DYNAMICCONFIGURATIONCONTROLLER_T70)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td colspan="3">Reserved</td><td colspan="2">FRCCMD</td><td>ALTSRC</td><td>RPTEN</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td rowspan="2">EVENT</td><td colspan="8">ENUMID (LSByte)</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>HOSTDEF</td><td colspan="7">ENUMID (MSbits)</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>OBJTYPE</td><td colspan="8">Object type element</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>OBJINST</td><td colspan="8">Object instance</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>DSTOFFSET</td><td colspan="8">Destination offset</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td rowspan="2">SRCOFFSET</td><td colspan="8">Source offset LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td colspan="8">Source offset MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>LENGTH</td><td colspan="8">Length offset</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables or disables the use of the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object. The object is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0.

RPTEN: Enables or disables the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object to report messages. Reporting is enabled if set to 1 , and disabled when set to 0 .

ALTSRC: This bit allows the host to select the location of the source data (see Table 6-48). The source data is selected from either the Dynamic Configuration Container T71 object with an associated offset, as defined in the SRCOFFSET field, or from the corresponding backed-up area in NVM.

TABLE 6-48: ALTSRC BIT - CONFIGURATION DATA SOURCES

<table><tr><td>Event Type</td><td>ALTSRC = 1</td><td>ALTSRC = 0</td></tr><tr><td>Single Edge Triggered Event</td><td>Configuration data read from NVM.</td><td>Configuration data read from Dynamic Configuration Container T71</td></tr><tr><td>Double Edge Triggered Event</td><td>Configuration data read from NVM on rising edge and from Dynamic Configuration Container T71 on falling edge</td><td>Configuration data read from Dynamic Configuration Container T71 on rising edge and from NVM on falling edge</td></tr></table>

FRCCMD: The FRCCMD control is used to allow the host to trigger the event configured in the EVENT Field. The FRCRISE and FRCFALL commands should be used accordingly to trigger on the corresponding edge of the configured event.

NOTE If more than one instance of the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 are configured to respond to the same event, using the FRCCMD control to force an event to be triggered on one instance will force all configured instances to respond as well.

Table 6-49 gives the values for the FRCCMD control.

TABLE 6-49: FRCCMD COMMAND CODES

<table><tr><td>FRCCMD</td><td>Command</td><td>Description</td></tr><tr><td>00</td><td>None</td><td>No trigger</td></tr><tr><td>01</td><td>FRCRISE</td><td>Triggers the event on a rising edge.</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>FRCFALL</td><td>Triggers the event on a falling edge.</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td>Reserved</td><td>-</td></tr></table>

EVENT Field

HOSTDEF: This field allows the host to specify the type of event: a device defined enumeration is specified if set to 0 , and a host defined enumeration is specified if set to 1 . This field must be used along with the FRCCMD control to trigger the host defined events. Host defined events have the behavior of double-edged events.

ENUMID: This field configures the event enumeration ID that is used to trigger an event for a particular instance of the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object. Table 6-50 lists the standard ENUMIDs available on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family. All other values have an undefined behavior unless the HOSTDEF bit is set to 1, in which case the ENUMID is a host-defined value.
