## OBJTYPE Field

This field specifies the Object Type of the object for which the configuration settings should be replaced when a specified event is triggered. This is the number after the "T" suffix at the end of the object's name.

Range: Depends on the objects available (see Section 1.6.2 "Object Instances")

## OBJINST FIELD

This field specifies the Object Instance for which the configuration settings should be replaced when a specified event is triggered.

Range: 0 to number of object instances minus 1 (see Section 1.6.2 "Object Instances")

## DSTOFFSET

This field specifies the starting Destination Offset of the first byte in the configuration area for the object for which the settings should be replaced. For example, to start at the GAIN field of the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object, DSTOFFSET would be 28.

Range: 0 to object size minus 1

## SRCOFFSET Field

This field specifies the starting Source Offset in the Dynamic Configuration Container T71 object from which to copy the source data. The maximum offset is Dynamic Configuration Container T71 size - 1 (see Section 6.11 "Dynamic Configuration Container T71 Object").

Range: 0 to Dynamic Configuration Container T71 size -1

## LENGTH Field

This field specifies the number of bytes to be written minus 1 (that is, the length of the data as an offset to the last byte).

Range: 0 to (Destination Object Size - Destination Object Offset) - 1

#### 6.10.3 CONFIGURATION CHECKS

A Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object causes a configuration check in the following circumstances:

- When the object is enabled

- If the object is enabled, when certain fields are changed

A configuration check may determine that a configuration error has occurred (for example, a setting is outside of its allowed range). This is signaled to the host and the device is halted until the error has been corrected. To fix an error, check that all object settings are within their allowed limits, as stated in the field descriptions.

Note that a configuration error is generated in the following situation:

- If the OBJTYPE is equal to 6 (Command Processor T6) and DSTOFFSET is less than 2. That is, if the destination object is the Command Processor T6, and the destination is either the RESET or BACKUPNV fields, a configuration error results.

TABLE 6-51: CONFIGURATION CHECKS FOR DYNAMIC CONFIGURATION CONTROLLER T70 (SPT_DYNAMICCONFIGURATIONCONTROLLER_T70)

<table><tr><td rowspan="2">Field</td><td colspan="2">Changing The Field Causes...</td><td rowspan="2">Effect of Configuration Checks On Field</td></tr><tr><td>Configuration Check</td><td>Automatic Recalibration</td></tr><tr><td>CTRL</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>EVENT</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>OBJTYPE</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>Error if specified object type is not supported.</td></tr><tr><td>OBJINST</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>Error if specified object instance is out of range.</td></tr><tr><td>DSTOFFSET</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>Error if specified destination offset is out of range of the specific object configuration area, or OBJTYPE = 6 and DSTOFFSET < 2.</td></tr><tr><td>SRCOFFSET</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>Error if specified address is out of range as defined in the Dynamic Configuration Container T71 object.</td></tr><tr><td>LENGTH</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>Error if specified LENGTH with DSTOFFSET is out of range, <br> or LENGTH with SRCOFFSET is out of range.</td></tr></table>

#### 6.10.4 MESSAGES

The message data for a Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object is shown in Table 6-52.

TABLE 6-52: MESSAGE DATA FOR DYNAMIC CONFIGURATION CONTROLLER T70 (SPT_DYNAMICCONFIGURATIONCONTROLLER_T70)

## STATUS Field

HANDLED: Indicates that an event has occurred and has been handled.

EVENTEDGE: Indicates a single-edge triggered event or the rising edge of a double-edge triggered event when set to 1 , or indicates a falling edge of a double-edge triggered event when set to 0 .

## mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family 1.0

### 6.11 Dynamic Configuration Container T71 Object

#### 6.11.1 INTRODUCTION

The Dynamic Configuration Container T71 object provides an area on the device for the user to store their own sets of configuration data that can be copied to other objects during run-time. The configurations are copied based on different events, as defined in the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object.

#### 6.11.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-53: CONFIGURATION FOR DYNAMIC CONFIGURATION CONTAINER T71 (SPT_DYNAMICCONFIGURATIONCONTAINER_T71)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0-(n-1)</td><td>DATAI</td><td colspan="8">Configuration Data</td></tr></table>

Note: \( \;n \) is the number of bytes for the Dynamic Configuration Container T71 object ( \( n = {200} \) in mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family)

## DATA[] Field

This field contains the configuration data. See Section 6.10 "Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 Object" for details on how this data is used.

### 6.12 Touch Event Trigger T79 Object

#### 6.12.1 INTRODUCTION

Each instance of the Touch Event Trigger T79 object configures a touch class trigger for use with a Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 object. It operates on the data received from the following objects:

- Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100

- Touch Suppression T42

- Passive Stylus T47

- Glove Detection T78

A Touch Event Trigger T79 object provides an interface that can be configured to trigger the following events based on the touch class:

- A positive edge Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 event on the detection of the touch class specified in the TOUCHCLASS field.

- A negative edge Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 event when the touch class specified in the TOUCHCLASS field is released and the timeout specified in the TCHRELTO field has elapsed.

On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family there are 3 instances of the Touch Event Trigger T79 object. These operate on touch data from the Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 object, or an associated signal processing object, as configured by the TOUCHCLASS field.

#### 6.12.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-54: CONFIGURATION FOR TOUCH EVENT TRIGGER T79 (SPT_TOUCHEVENTTRIGGER_T79)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td colspan="7">Reserved</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>TOUCHCLASS</td><td colspan="8">Touch class trigger</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>TCHRELTO</td><td colspan="8">Touch release timeout</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>NUMTCHTHR</td><td></td><td>Reserved</td><td></td><td colspan="5">NUMTCHTHR</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables or disables the use of this instance of the Touch Event Trigger T79 object. The instance is enabled if set to 1 , and disabled if set to 0 .

## TOUCHCLASS Field

This field specifies the touch class that triggers the Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 events on detection or release. The Touch Event Trigger T79 object supports the touch classes listed in Table 6-55.

TABLE 6-55: TOUCH CLASSES

<table><tr><td>Code</td><td>Mode</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Palm Touch (other touch classes might also be present)</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Passive Stylus and Palm Touch</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>Passive Stylus</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>Passive Stylus or Palm Touch</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>Any Touch (including all types of touches)</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td>Glove Touch (other touch classes might also be present)</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td>Finger Touch (other touch classes might also be present)</td></tr><tr><td>14</td><td>Finger Touch Only (no other touch class present)</td></tr><tr><td>All other values</td><td>Reserved; undefined behavior may occur</td></tr></table>

## TCHRELTO Field

This field specifies Touch Release Timeout. This is the timeout after which a Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 negative edge event is triggered on a touch release that has the touch class specified in TCHCLASS. The Touch Release Timeout is specified in units of \( {200}\mathrm{\;{ms}} \) .

Range: 0 to 255

## NUMTCHTHR Field

NUMTCHTHR: Specifies the Number of Touches Threshold. This is the minimum number of any touches, of which one must satisfy the selected TOUCHCLASS for this instance of the Touch Event Trigger T79 object, that will trigger the associated Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 event (see Table 6-55). The range for this field is 0 to the maximum number of touches (16 on mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family), where the default value of 0 means 1.

NUMTCHTHR Range: 0 (1), 1 to 16

### 6.13 Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 Object

#### 6.13.1 INTRODUCTION

An Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 object allows the setting of gain and thresholds for self capacitance measurements to generate auxiliary touch data for use by other objects.

Specifically the Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 object generates self capacitance touch data, which is then used by the Retransmission Compensation T80 object to help with retransmission errors, water immunity and gloved touches.

See Appendix A "Measurement Processing" for more details on how the Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 object operates with other objects.

#### 6.13.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-56: CONFIGURATION FOR AUXILIARY TOUCH CONFIGURATION T104 (SPT_AUXTOUCHCONFIG_T104)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td colspan="2">Reserved</td><td>DEFMEASACTV</td><td>DEFMEASIDLE</td><td colspan="3">Reserved</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>XGAIN</td><td colspan="8">X axis gain</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>XTCHTHR</td><td colspan="8">X axis touch threshold</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>XTCHHYST</td><td colspan="8">X axis touch hysteresis</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>XINTTHR</td><td colspan="8">X axis internal threshold</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>XINTHYST</td><td colspan="8">X axis internal hysteresis</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>YGAIN</td><td colspan="8">Y axis gain</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>YTCHTHR</td><td colspan="8">Y axis touch threshold</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>YTCHHYST</td><td colspan="8">Y axis touch hysteresis</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td>YINTHR</td><td colspan="8">Y axis internal threshold</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td>YINTHYST</td><td colspan="8">Y axis internal hysteresis</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables or disables the use of the Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 object. The object is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0 .

The MEASALLOW field in the Acquisition Configuration T8 object must be set appropriately to allow self capacitance touches in order for the Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 to operate correctly.

NOTE A tune should be performed using the Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 object after enabling the Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 object or modifying its configuration (see "CMD Field").

DEFMEASIDLE: If this bit is set to 1, self capacitance measurements are included in the Default Measurement types in Idle mode (see Section A.2.1 "Default Measurements").

DEFMEASACTV: If this bit is set to 1, self capacitance measurements are included in the Default Measurement types in Active mode.

## XGAIN Field

This field sets the X Axis Gain. This is the gain of the analog circuits in front of the analog to digital converter (ADC) for X axis self capacitance measurements. The default range is 0 to 29.

The default range should be sufficient for most applications. However, using Gain * 2 mode may help improve moisture immunity performance. To enable Gain * 2 mode, set XGAIN bit 7 to 1. This will add additional settings in the range to 128 to 157.

For more information on choosing a suitable gain value, refer to maXTouch U Series Tuning Guide.

Range: 0 to 29, 128 to 157 (Gain × 2 mode)

mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family 1.0

## XTCHTHR Field

This field specifies the X Axis Touch Threshold in 8-bit deltas. This is the threshold above which X axis nodes are marked as above threshold or in detect.

Range: 0 to 255

Typical: 80

## XTCHHYST Field

This field specifies the X Axis Touch Hysteresis in 8-bit deltas. This is used to specify a difference in threshold which would cause nodes in detect (based upon XTCHTHR) to go out of detect.

XTCHHYST is capped internally to (XTCHTHR × 0.75). A hysteresis greater than 75% of the X Axis Touch Threshold is therefore not possible. Note that, under normal circumstances, it is not recommended to set the hysteresis to more than 25% of the X Axis Touch Threshold (XTCHTHR), as this can cause potential problems during touch lift off, double taps, and noise handling.

A value of 0 means there is no hysteresis.

Range: 0 (no hysteresis), 1 to XTCHTHR × 0.75

Typical: 20

## XINTTHR Field

This field specifies the X Axis Internal Threshold in 8-bit deltas. This is the threshold above which X axis nodes are marked as above the internal threshold or in detect at a lower threshold.

Range: 0 to 255

Typical: 20

## XINTHYST Field

This field specifies the X Axis Internal Hysteresis in 8-bit deltas. This is used to specify a difference in threshold which would cause nodes in detect (based upon XINTTHR) to go out of detect.

XINTHYST is capped internally to (XINTTHR \( \times  {0.75} \) ). A hysteresis greater than 75% of the X Axis Internal Threshold is therefore not possible. Note that, under normal circumstances, it is not recommended to set the hysteresis to more than 25% of the X Axis Internal Threshold (XINTTHR), as this can cause potential problems during touch lift off, double taps, and noise handling.

A value of 0 means there is no hysteresis.

Range: 0 (no hysteresis), 1 to XINTTHR × 0.75

Typical: 5

## YGAIN Field

This field sets the Y Axis Gain. This is the gain of the analog circuits in front of the analog to digital converter (ADC) for Y axis self capacitance measurements. The default range is 0 to 29.

The default range should be sufficient for most applications. However, using Gain x 2 mode may help improve moisture immunity performance. To enable Gain x 2 mode, set YGAIN bit 7 to 1. This will add additional settings in the range to 128 to 157.

For more information on choosing a suitable gain value, refer to maXTouch U Series Tuning Guide.

Range: 0 to 29, 128 to 157 (Gain × 2 mode)

## YTCHTHR Field

This field specifies the Y Axis Touch Threshold in 8-bit deltas. This is the threshold above which Y axis nodes are marked as above threshold or in detect.

Range: 0 to 255

Typical: 80

## YTCHHYST Field

This field specifies the Y Axis Touch Hysteresis in 8-bit deltas. This is used to specify a difference in threshold which would cause nodes in detect (based upon YTCHTHR) to go out of detect.

YTCHHYST is capped internally to (YTCHTHR × 0.75). A hysteresis greater than 75% of the Y Axis Touch Threshold is therefore not possible. Note that, under normal circumstances, it is not recommended to set the hysteresis to more than 25% of the Y Axis Touch Threshold (YTCHTHR), as this can cause potential problems during touch lift off, double taps, and noise handling.

A value of 0 means there is no hysteresis.

Range: 0 (no hysteresis), 1 to YTCHTHR × 0.75

Typical: 20

## YINTTHR Field

This field specifies the Y Axis Internal Threshold in 8-bit deltas. This is the threshold above which Y axis nodes are marked as above the internal threshold or in detect at a lower threshold.

Range: 0 to 255

Typical: 20

## YINTHYST Field

This field specifies the Y axis Internal Hysteresis in 8-bit deltas. This is used to specify a difference in threshold which would cause nodes in detect (based upon YINTTHR) to go out of detect.

YINTHYST is capped internally to (YINTTHR \( \times  {0.75} \) ). A hysteresis greater than 75% of the Y Axis Internal Threshold is therefore not possible. Note that, under normal circumstances, it is not recommended to set the hysteresis to more than 25% of the Y Axis Internal Threshold (YINTTHR), as this can cause potential problems during touch lift off, double taps, and noise handling.

A value of 0 means there is no hysteresis.

Range: 0 (no hysteresis), 1 to YINTTHR × 0.75

Typical: 5

#### 6.13.3 CONFIGURATION CHECKS

The Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 object causes a configuration check to be performed in the following circumstances:

- When the object is enabled (that is, the ENABLE bit is set in the CTRL field)

- If the object is enabled, when certain fields are changed

In addition, some fields may cause an automatic recalibration to be performed.

A configuration check may determine that a configuration error has occurred (for example, if a setting is set outside of its allowed range or a conflict has occurred between two settings). This is signaled to the host (see Section 3.3 "Command Processor T6 Object"). The device halts until the error has been corrected. To fix the error, check that all the object settings are within their allowed limits, as stated in the field descriptions.

TABLE 6-57: CONFIGURATION CHECKS FOR AUXILIARY TOUCH CONFIGURATION T104 (SPT_AUXTOUCHCONFIG_T104)

<table><tr><td rowspan="2">Field</td><td colspan="2">Changing The Field Causes...</td><td rowspan="2">Effect of Configuration Checks On Field</td></tr><tr><td>Configuration Check</td><td>Automatic Recalibration</td></tr><tr><td>CTRL</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes (1)</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>XGAIN</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>XTCHTHR</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>XTCHHYST</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>XINTTHR</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>XINTHYST</td><td>Yes</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr></table>

TABLE 6-57: CONFIGURATION CHECKS FOR AUXILIARY TOUCH CONFIGURATION T104 (SPT_AUXTOUCHCONFIG_T104)

Note 1: If the ENABLE bit is toggled on or off.

### 6.14 Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 Object

#### 6.14.1 INTRODUCTION

The Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 object provides configuration for self capacitance measurements employed on the device.

#### 6.14.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-58: CONFIGURATION FOR SELF CAPACITANCE GLOBAL CONFIGURATION T109 (SPT_SELFCAPGLOBALCONFIG_T109)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td>DISMEASY</td><td>DISMEASX</td><td colspan="2">Reserved</td><td>DISPRECHARGE</td><td>SNGLENDEN</td><td>RPTEN</td><td>Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>CMDONRESET</td><td colspan="8">Command performed on reset</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>CMD</td><td colspan="8">Command</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>8</td><td>TUNECFG</td><td colspan="5">Reserved</td><td colspan="3">EXTRATUNITER</td></tr><tr><td>9</td><td rowspan="2">TUNPARAM[0]</td><td colspan="8">Host side tuning parameters 0 LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>10</td><td colspan="8">Host side tuning parameters 0 MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>11</td><td rowspan="2">TUNPARAM[1]</td><td colspan="8">Host side tuning parameters 1 LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>12</td><td colspan="8">Host side tuning parameters 1 MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>13</td><td rowspan="2">TUNPARAM[2]</td><td colspan="8">Host side tuning parameters 2 LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>14</td><td colspan="8">Host side tuning parameters 2 MSByte</td></tr><tr><td>15</td><td rowspan="2">TUNPARAM[3]</td><td colspan="8">Host side tuning parameters 3 LSByte</td></tr><tr><td>16</td><td colspan="8">Host side tuning parameters 3 MSByte</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

RPTEN: Allows the object to send status messages to the host through the Message Processor T5 object. Reporting is enabled if set to 1 , and disabled if set to 0 .

SNGLENDEN: Enables Single Ended Measurement.

NOTE This control is for use only during design, under the guidance of Microchip field engineers, to help tune the product for characterization. It should not be used in production. This control should be left at its default value of 0 , unless advised otherwise by Microchip.

DISPRECHARGE: Disables Pre-charge. If this bit is set to 1, it disables the pre-charge to AVDD (rising edge) or GND (falling edge) before the integration phase of a self capacitance measurement pulse. This applies to all self capacitance measurements.

DISMEASX and DISMEASY: Disable Self Capacitance Measurements on the X or Y axis. If one of these bits is set to 1, all self capacitance measurements on the corresponding axis are disabled. If one of these bits is set to 0, all self capacitance measurements on the corresponding axis can be made. It is not recommended to disable measurements on both axes (that is DISMEASX = 1 and DISMEASY = 1); one axis should always remain enabled.

NOTE DISMEASX must be set to 0 (that is, the X axis measurement must not be disabled) if the Driven Shield Signal Limit test is in use (see Self Test Signal Limits T12 "CTRL Field").

Note that the ability to disable self capacitance measurements on the X or Y axis depends on other configuration settings:

- Acquisition Configuration T8: MEASALLOW (see Acquisition Configuration T8 "MEASALLOW Field")

- Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104: CTRL ENABLE (see Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 "CTRL Field")

- Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113: CTRL ENABLE and CTRL ALTAXISEN (see Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 "CTRL Field")

In particular, setting DISMEASX and DISMEASY should be done in conjunction with the Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 CTRL ALTAXISEN control.

## CMDONRESET Field

This field schedules the given command on reset. See Table 6-59 for command values.

Range: See Table 6-59

CMD Field

This field schedules the given command.

The command field is cleared after the command has been actioned.

Range: See Table 6-59

#### 6.14.3 CONFIGURATION CHECKS

A Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 object causes a configuration check to be performed in the following circumstances:

- When certain fields are changed

In addition, some fields may cause an automatic recalibration to be performed.

A configuration check may determine that a configuration error has occurred (for example, if a setting is set outside of its allowed range or a conflict has occurred between two settings). This is signaled to the host (see Section 3.3 "Command Processor T6 Object"). The device halts until the error has been corrected. To fix the error, check that all the object settings are within their allowed limits, as stated in the field descriptions. While the object is disabled, however, potential configuration errors are allowed.

## CMD Field

This field reports the command that was processed and has caused this message (see "CMDONRESET Field" and "CMD Field").

## ERRORCODE Field

This field reports the success/error code. An error code of 0 means that there is no error (success). Otherwise, a non-zero indicates the error resulting from the command that caused this message (see Table 6-64).

TABLE 6-64: ERROR CODES

<table><tr><td>Command</td><td>Error Codes</td><td>Order (1)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="6">1 – Tune</td><td>0x04 – Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 and/or Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 not enabled or self capacitance touch measurements not allowed in Acquisition Configuration T8.</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>0x01 – Self capacitance touch measurements tuning initialization failed because the signals saturated. <br> Indicates a problem with the sensor design.</td><td>2</td></tr><tr><td>0x02 – Self capacitance measurements tuning process could not complete successfully due to excessive loading of the sensor used. <br> May indicate a problem with the sensor.</td><td>3</td></tr><tr><td>0x05 – Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 not enabled or single-ended self capacitance measurements not allowed in Acquisition Configuration T8. <br> Tuning of single-ended self capacitance measurements has been excluded.</td><td>4</td></tr><tr><td>0x03 – Single-ended self capacitance measurements tuning process was successful but single-ended self capacitance tuning was out of range. <br> Further tuning may be possible. Refer to the maXTouch U Series Tuning Guide for more details.</td><td>5</td></tr><tr><td>0 – Tuning successful</td><td>6</td></tr></table>

Note 1: Tune command error codes are listed in order of precedence: high (1) to low (6). Error codes for other commands have no order of precedence.

The error codes are generated in the order shown in Table 6-64 as the tuning process proceeds. This means that higher precedence errors may mask lower order errors. For example, an error code of 0x04 may mask one or more of the lower order errors (0x01, 0x02, 0x05 and/or 0x03 in order).

### 6.16 Self Capacitance Configuration T111 Object

#### 6.16.1 INTRODUCTION

The Self Capacitance Configuration T111 object provides configuration for self capacitance measurements (see Appendix A "Measurement Processing"), including pulse synchronization during self capacitance measurements.

On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family there are 2 instances of the Self Capacitance Configuration T111 object (see Table 6-67 for details).

TABLE 6-67: SELF CAPACITANCE CONFIGURATION T111 INSTANCES

<table><tr><td>Instance</td><td>Purpose</td></tr><tr><td>Instance 0</td><td>Used to configure self capacitance touch measurements. Settings for this instance use a subset of the configuration fields (see Table 6-68 on page 239).</td></tr><tr><td>Instance 1</td><td>Used to configure self capacitance single-ended measurements. Settings for this instance use a subset of the configuration fields (see Table 6-69 on page 240).</td></tr></table>

Note: Each instance configures a particular measurement type and the settings for that instance are applied to all measurements of that type for use by other objects. Therefore, the controls for each instance need to be tuned to values that are appropriate across all touch objects that use those measurements.

Self capacitance measurements are required for single touch measurements when self capacitance measurements are selected as the primary measurement type. Self capacitance data is also used to augment the mutual capacitance data to help cope with retransmission and moisture issues (see Section 5.13 "Retransmission Compensation T80 Object").

See Appendix A "Measurement Processing" for more details on how the Self Capacitance Configuration T111 object operates with other objects.

##### 6.16.1.1 Self Capacitance Pulses

The pulse for a self capacitance measurement is outlined in Figure 6-7.

With reference to Figure 6-7, the Integration Time is specified by INTTIME (see "INTTIME Field"). The Delay Time is the additional time by which a pulse is extended after the integration time has completed, and is specified by DELAYTIME (see "DELAYTIME Field"). The Gap Time is the extra time provided by the associated Self Capacitance Noise Suppression T108 object.

These three parameters are used to derive the Mark Time and the Space Time. The Mark Time is the sum of the Integration Time, the Gap Time, and the Delay Time. The Space Time is equal to the Mark Time.

When there is no pulse synchronization, the length of the pulse is simply the Mark Time plus the Space Time. When pulse synchronization is applied, however, the timing of the pulses is determined by the frequency of the synchronization pulses. Consequently, the observed Delay Time is extended to the next synchronization pulse (see Figure 6-8).

SELF CAPACITANCE MEASUREMENT PULSE - NO PULSE SYNCHRONIZATION

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_235.jpg?x=563&y=1597&w=776&h=449&r=0"/>

NOTE: The pulse shape is shown for guidance only. The shape may vary between devices, although the timing principles are the same.

SELF CAPACITANCE MEASUREMENT PULSE - WITH PULSE SYNCHRONIZATION

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_236.jpg?x=386&y=316&w=1130&h=600&r=0"/>

##### 6.16.1.2 Analog-to-Digital Conversions

The matrix axes are sampled one at a time (depending on the hardware there may be more than one burst per axis), with at least 2 analog-to-digital conversions (ADCs) performed on each axis in turn. Note that on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family, the X axis is scanned twice: first the odd numbered X lines are scanned and then the even numbered X lines.

The number of ADCs per X line is specified by the ACTVSYNCSPERL/IDLESYNCSPERL and ADCSPERSYNC fields.

The number of ADCs per line is a nominal value only. Other objects can influence the ADCs per line setting under specific circumstances. Specifically, if Self Capacitance Noise Suppression T108 is enabled, ADCs per line values from this object (selected based upon state) will be used for Self Capacitance Touch measurements instead of the T111 value. Note that Single-ended Self Capacitance measurements always use the Self Capacitance Configuration T111 value and are not subject to the Self Capacitance Noise Suppression T108 values.

NOTE The minimum Active/Idle ADCs per line is saturated to 2. Therefore, if less than 2 ADCs per line is configured, 2 ADCs per line will be used.

6.16.1.3 Pulse Synchronization

MPORTANT! Pulse Synchronization functionality on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family is not considered UL/IEC 60730 Class B compliant. Therefore, the device should not be configured to use Pulse Synchronization in a UL/IEC 60730 Class B product.

NOTE The SYNC line can be used for either pulse synchronization or frame synchronization (see "SYNC Field"), but not both. If the SYNC line is used for pulse synchronization functionality, then it cannot be used for frame synchronization.

The ADCSPERSYNC field determines how the ADCs are synchronized to the SYNC line (see Figure 6-9 on page 239):

- If the ADCSPERSYNC field is set to zero, then no pulse synchronization occurs.

- If the ADCSPERSYNC field is set to 1, then pulse synchronization occurs. In this case, the rising and falling edges of each ADC are synchronized to the falling edge of the SYNC signal.

- If the ADCSPERSYNC field is set to a value of 2 or above, the ADCs are arranged in "Sync Groups". The number of ADCs per Sync Group is (ADCSPERSYNC - 1). In this case, the ACTVSYNCSPERL and IDLESYNCSPERL fields determine the number of Sync Groups per X line. Thus, the total number of ADCs per X is equivalent to:

- (ADCSPERSYNC - 1) * ACTVSYNCSPERL or IDLESYNCSPERL

- with a minimum value of 2 .

Note the following:

- Pulse synchronization for Self capacitance measurements is enabled for each measurement type independently, according to which Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instances are configured. To enable pulse synchronization on mutual capacitance measurements, see Section 6.8 "CTE Configuration T46 Object".

- If pulse synchronization is turned on (that is, ADCSPERSYNC is non-zero), GPIO0 cannot be configured by the GPIO Configuration T19 object. GPIO0 must be set as an input, or the GPIO Configuration T19 object disabled, for the pulse synchronization to work.

- If there is a requirement to toggle pulse synchronization on and off at run time, the device must be configured and backed up with pulse synchronization enabled in either Self Capacitance Configuration T111 or CTE Configuration T46. This ensures that the device will start up with pulse synchronization enabled for at least one measurement type and the SYNC pin is latched for use. This prevents the pin from being used for other uses.

- If the system has been configured to use pulse synchronization and there is a failure to detect a SYNC signal, the default behavior of the system is to continue measurements unsynchronized using user-configured timing. If this behavior is not required, CTE Configuration T46 CFG SYNCLOSSMODE can be set to 1 to pause measurements altogether while pulse synchronization is absent (see CTE Configuration T46 "CFG Field"). When a SYNC signal is subsequently detected, pulse synchronization will be re-enabled and the measurements will continue with synchronized ADCs. Note that CTE Configuration T46 CFG SYNCLOSSMODE has an effect on all mutual and self capacitance measurements.

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_238.jpg?x=239&y=203&w=1410&h=1355&r=0"/>

Notes:

- Both axes are burst simultaneously but measurements are on one axis only

- The pulse shape is shown for guidance only. The shape may vary between devices, although the timing principles are the same.

sources="240"><td>19</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>20</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>21</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>22</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>23</td><td sources="240"><td>25</td><td>ADCSPERSYNC</td><td></td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="6">ADCSPERSYNC</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>26</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>27</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>28</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>29</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>30</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr sources="240"><td>31</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

LFCOMPEN: (Touch data instance only) Enables Low Frequency Compensation.

If this bit is set to 1, low frequency compensation is performed on the measurement. In this case, the Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 tuning procedure will perform 3 phases of tuning for the self capacitance differential (assuming that there is enough storage space within Self Capacitance Tuning Parameters T110). Note the following:

- The number of ADCs per line should be set to a multiple of 3 (see "IDLESYNCSPERL Field" and "ACTVSYNCSPERL Field"), but the device will constrain this internally if the ADCs per line is not set appropriately.

- An additional sample is added per scan, so the amount of pulses seen is:

((ADCs_per_line / 3) × 3) + 1

If this bit is set to 0, low frequency compensation is not applied to the measurement and the tuning procedure will run as normal. In this case, the Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 tuning procedure will perform only a single phase of tuning.

NOTE If the Driven Shield Signal Limits Test is enabled for use (Self Test Signal Limits T12 CTRL DSTESTEN = 1), low frequency compensation cannot be used. Low frequency compensation must therefore be disabled by setting LFCOMPEN to 0 if the Driven Shield Signal Limits Test is enabled.

DISDCCORR: (Touch data instance only) If this bit is set to 0, the self capacitance single-ended measurement data is used to correct the DC level of the self capacitance touch data in the case when it appears that the self capacitance touch DC level is incorrectly too high and might therefore create false touches. If this bit is set to 1, this DC correction is disabled. Disabling DC Correction should only be used in cases where the self capacitance single-ended data is unreliable for this purpose.

NOTE To correct the DC level of the self capacitance touch data, one of the following two options should be used:

- Use the Self Capacitance Single-ended measurement data by setting DISDCCORR = 0

- Use the Lens Bending T65 Lens Bending Self Capacitance Instances (that is, enable and configure Lens Bending T65 Instances 1 and 2)

Note that these two options should not be used together as the combined behavior is undefined. In addition, if neither option is used, the DC level will be poor.

## DBGCTRL Field

This field allows different debug data types to be enabled or disabled for use with the hardware debug interface. Note that the Command Processor T6 DEBUGCTRL2 DBGOBJMODEEN bit must be set to 1 for this to work. See "DEBUGCTRL2 Field" for more information on the debug data for the hardware debug interface.

DELTASEN: (Self Capacitance Touch and Single-ended data instances only) If this bit is set to 1, self capacitance deltas are output by the hardware debug interface.

REFSEN: (Self Capacitance Touch and Single-ended data instances only) If this bit is set to 1, self capacitance references are output by the hardware debug interface.

SIGSEN: (Self Capacitance Touch and Single-ended data instances only) If this bit is set to 1, self capacitance signals are output by the hardware debug interface.

RAWDATAEN: (Self Capacitance Touch data instance only) If this bit is set to 1, raw data values are output by the hardware debug interface in addition to the processed data.

DCEN: (Self Capacitance Touch data instance only) If this bit is set to 1, DC debug data is output by the hardware debug interface.

## INTTIME Field

This field specifies the Integration Time in 24 MHz clock cycles (41.67 ns), where the default value of 0 means 36 (1.5 μs).

Range: 0 (36), 1 to 255

## DELAYTIME Field

This field specifies the Delay Time in 24 MHz clock cycles (41.67 ns). This is the length of additional time that a pulse is extended by after the integration time has completed. The default value of 0 means \( {36}\left( {{1.5\mu }\mathrm{s}}\right) \) .

Range: 0 (36), 1 to 255

## IDLESYNCSPERL Field

This field determines the number of ADCs per Sensor Line in Idle mode. The range for this field is 0 to 255, where a value of 0 means 8 .

See Section 6.16.1 "Introduction" for more information on how this field helps determine the actual number of ADCs per Line

Range: 0 (8), 1 to 255

## ACTVSYNCSPERL Field

This field determines the number of ADCs per Sensor Line in Active mode. The range for this field is 0 to 255, where a value of 0 means 8 .

See Section 6.16.1 "Introduction" for more information on how this field helps determine the actual number of ADCs per Line

Range: 0 (8), 1 to 255

## DRIFT Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

The default behavior of this field is to provide the interval (specified in 200 ms increments) between drift operations for self capacitance bassed references. A drift operation samples the deltas after a cycle, and "moves" the references (per node) towards those deltas. This allows for small variations in operating conditions, such as temperature changes. The amount to drift is specific to the measurement type, but typically a drift "moves" the references by 4 to 8 16-bit delta counts.

The range is 0 to 255 in 200 ms increments, where the default value of 0 means 5 (1 second). A value of 255 (disabled) is not recommended for this field.

Range: 0 (5), 1 to 254, 255 (disabled)

## DRIFTST Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field specifies the Drift Suspend Time. This is the duration for which drift is suspended after any touches have been removed. See the mutual capacitance handling of the "DRIFTST Field" for more information on the Drift Suspend Time.

DRIFTST is configured in units of 200 ms, where a value of zero means 10 (2 seconds).

Range: 0 (10), 1 to 255

## CALRECSTR Field

This field configures the Calibration Recovery Strength.

The Calibration Recovery process causes an automatic calibration when the system decides that a calibrated in touch has been removed from the sensor. This field controls how aggressive that process is for self-capacitance touch data. Low values will increase the probability of a system calibration; high values will decrease this probability. A value of 255 disables this feature, and the default value of 0 means 30 .

Note that the tuning data can be output through the Diagnostic Debug T37 object using the Command Processor T6 DIAGNOSTIC command (see Section 2.2 "Diagnostic Debug T37 Object" and "DIAGNOSTIC Field"). Note that this must be enabled using the Acquisition Configuration T8 CFG CALRECTUN control (see "CFG Field").

Range: 0 (30), 1 to 254, 255 (disabled)

## INRUSHCFG Field

YRESISTOR/XRESISTOR: Controls the selection of the inrush current resistors for the measurement type associated with the object instance. The value specified controls the selection for all X or Y line measurements (as appropriate). The value specified controls the selection for all X or Y lines (as appropriate).

YRESISTOR/XRESISTOR Range: See Table 6-70.

TABLE 6-70: YRESISTOR AND XRESISTOR VALUES

<table><tr><td>YRESISTOR/XRESISTOR Setting</td><td>Resistor Value</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>50Ω (default)</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>71Ω</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>117Ω</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>180Ω</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>276Ω</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>424Ω</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>651Ω</td></tr><tr><td>7</td><td>1KΩ</td></tr></table>

## ALTINTTIMEX Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field specifies the Alternative X Axis Measurement Integration Time in 24 MHz clock cycles (41.67 ns). This allows different integration times to be specified for the self capacitance touch and hover X and Y measurements. Note that this field does not apply to self capacitance single-ended measurements.

If this field is set to zero, the INTTIME setting is used for both X and Y measurements (see "INTTIME Field").

If this field is set to a non-zero value then the specified value is used for X measurements, and the INTTIME field setting is used for the Y measurement.

Note that, if ALTINTTIMEX is being used, it is important to make sure that the DELAYTIME and ALTDELAYTIMEX are adjusted such that the following condition is met (see "DELAYTIME Field" and "ALTDELAYTIMEX Field"):

INTTIME + DELAYTIME = ALTINTTIMEX + ALTDELAYTIMEX

Otherwise external noise handling performance will be impacted.

Range: See Table 6-71

TABLE 6-71: ALTINTTIMEX VALUES

<table><tr><td>Value</td><td>X Measurements</td><td>Y Measurements</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td colspan="2">The INTTIME setting is used for both X and Y measurements</td></tr><tr><td>1 to 255</td><td>ALTINTTIMEX specifies an alternative integration time for X measurements</td><td>The INTTIME setting is used for Y measurements.</td></tr></table>

## ALTDELAYTIMEX Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field specifies the Alternative X Axis Measurement Delay Time in 24 MHz clock cycles (41.67 ns). This allows different delay times to be specified for the self capacitance touch X and Y measurements. Note that this field does not apply to self capacitance single-ended measurements.

If this field is set to zero, the DELAYTIME setting is used for both X and Y measurements (see "DELAYTIME Field").

If this field is set to a non-zero value then the specified value is used for X measurements, and the DELAYTIME field setting is used for the Y measurement.

Note that, if an alternative integration time is being used (see "ALTINTTIMEX Field"), ALTDELAYTIME value must be set such that the two burst frequencies match.

Range: 0 (DELAYTIME used for both X and Y measurements),

1 to 255

## DCDRIFT Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field controls the DC Drift Interval for DC correction. The drift intervals for other measurement type instances are stored in other objects.

Signals can drift because of changes in the nature of the components and materials over time and temperature. It is crucial that such drift is compensated for, otherwise false detections and sensitivity shifts can occur.

Drift compensation is performed by adjusting the reference level. The rate of adjustment is performed slowly, otherwise the incorrect DC levels may introduce erroneous touch detections and calibrations. The DCDRIFT field is configured in increments of \( {200}\mathrm{\;{ms}} \) ,where the default value of 0 means 5 (1 second). A value of 255 disables drift.

Range: 0 (5), 1 to 254, 255 (disabled)

## DCFILTER Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch

data.

This field provides the DC Filter controls.

IIREN: Enables the IIR Filter. The filter is enabled if this bit is set to 1, and disabled if it is set to 0.

IIRCOEF: Specifies the DC IIR Filter Coefficient. The units are 2s exponent of filter coefficient.

IIRCOEF Range: 0 to 7

IIRCOEF Typical: 1

SLEWEN: Enables the Slew Rate Filter. The slew rate filter is enabled if this bit is set to 1, and disabled if it is set to 0 .

SLEWACC: Enables the Slew Rate Filter Accelerator. The accelerator is enabled if this bit is set to 1, and disabled if it is set to 0 .

## DCCALRECSTR Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field configures the DC Calibration Recovery Strength.

The DC Calibration Recovery process causes an automatic calibration when the system decides that the overall touch level has become negative. This field controls how aggressive that process is for the self capacitance DC level. Low values will increase the probability of a system calibration; high values will decrease this probability. A value of 255 disables this feature. The default value of 0 means 30.

Note that the tuning data can be output through the Diagnostic Debug T37 object using the Command Processor T6 DIAGNOSTIC command (see Section 2.2 "Diagnostic Debug T37 Object" and "DIAGNOSTIC Field"). Note that this must be enabled using the Acquisition Configuration T8 CFG CALRECTUN control (see "CFG Field").

NOTE If DC calibration is enabled (that is, not equal to 255), then the self capacitance touch measurement must be allowed using Acquisition Configuration T8 MEASALLOW (see "MEASALLOW Field").

Range: 0 (30), 1 to 254, 255 (disabled)

## DCCALERRRATIO Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field configures the DC Calibration Error Ratio. This is the proportion (in units of 1/256) of the difference between the DC level estimates for the single-ended and auxiliary touch measurements. This difference is compared against the calibration recovery strength in order to trigger a calibration.

Range: 0 to 255

## SYNCDELAY Field

This 16-bit field specifies the delay from when the SYNC edge occurs to when the positive/negative edge of the self capacitance pulse is generated.

The delay is specified in units of the CTE clock period (20 ns; 50 MHz), where a value of 0 means no additional delay.

Range: 0 (no additional delay), 1 to 65534

## ADCSPERSYNC Field

OTE If synchronization is turned on (that is, ADCSPERSYNC is non-zero), GPIO0 cannot be configured by the GPIO Configuration T19 object. GPIO0 must be set as an input, or the GPIO Configuration T19 object disabled, for the CTE Configuration T46 pulse synchronization to work.

ADCSPERSYNC: Determines whether or not the ADC conversions are synchronized to the SYNC pin for self capacitance measurements. To enable pulse synchronization on mutual capacitance measurements, see Section 6.8 "CTE Configuration T46 Object".

A value of 0 means no synchronization is required (that is, it is not synchronized to the input signal on the SYNC pin).

A value of 1 synchronizes the rising and falling edges of each ADC to the falling edge of the SYNC signal (see Figure 6-9 on page 239 for an example).

A value greater than 1 determines the number (value minus 1) of ADCs per Sync Group.

Note that if there is a requirement to toggle pulse synchronization on and off at run time, the device must be configured and backed up with pulse synchronization enabled in either Self Capacitance Configuration T111 or CTE Configuration T46. This ensures that the device will start up with pulse synchronization enabled for at least one measurement type and the SYNC pin is latched for use. This prevents the pin from being used for other uses.

Range: 0 (no synchronization),

1 (ADCs synchronized to SYNC)

2 to 63

## DCGAINSF Field

NOTE This field is used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field configures the DC Gain Scaling Factor. This is the scaling factor used in gain calculations associated with the system-provided DC level. The value is used to scale the magnitude of the input DC level so that it better matches the estimates based upon other self capacitance touch measurements.

A smaller value should be used if the DC level exceeds the estimate from other self capacitance measurements; a larger value should be used if the DC level is less than the estimate from other self capacitance measurements. It may be beneficial to re-tune this value if the gain of the self capacitance measurements is changed.

The value for this field is a signed 8-bit number, where -128 represents a scaling factor of 50%, 0 represents a scaling factor of 100% and +127 represents a scaling factor of 150%.

Range: -128 to +127

## DCTHRX Field

NOTE This field is used only by the Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field configures the Self Capacitance DC Threshold for X axis measurements against which the DC estimate is compared for leaving the low power idle state.

Range: 0 to 255

## DCTHRY Field

NOTE This field is used only by the Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field configures the Self Capacitance DC Threshold for Y axis measurements against which the DC estimate is compared for leaving the low power idle state.

Range: 0 to 255

## DCIDLESLEWMIN Field

NOTE This field is used only by the Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

This field configures a minimum slew rate applied to the DC estimate for the measurement controlled by this Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance. The slew rate can reduce to one count per acquisition cycle in quiet conditions and thus will increase first touch latency greatly when the idle default measurement is self capacitance single ended (see the DEFMEASIDLE control in the Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 "CTRL Field"). The slew rate must allow enough change in the estimate to allow the DC threshold to be reached. A value of approximately (3 * DCTHRX) or (3 * DCTHRY), as appropriate, should result in a first touch latency very similar to that when the default idle mode is MUTUALTCH or SELFTCH.

Range: 0 (1), 1 to 255

DCPROCTHRX and DCPROCTHRY Fields

NOTE These fields are used only by Self Capacitance Configuration T111 instance 0 for self capacitance touch data.

These fields set the DC Level Processing Threshold for the X and Y lines. This is the threshold used for processing DC level estimates for the X and Y lines (for example, for use by the Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 algorithms). If the threshold is greater than or equal to DCPROCTHRX/DCPROCTHRY, the DC level processing is done. The threshold is specified in 8-bit delta values, where the default value of 0 effectively means always perform the processing.

Range: 0 to 255

#### 6.16.3 CONFIGURATION CHECKS

An instance of the Self Capacitance Configuration T111 object may cause an automatic recalibration to be performed when certain fields are changed.

mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family 1.0

### 6.17 Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 Object

#### 6.17.1 INTRODUCTION

A Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 object is used to set the gain for a particular self capacitance single-ended measurement to generate data for use by other objects.

The current use of this object on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family is to make it possible for the Acquisition Configuration T8 object to trigger a recalibration when an antitouch is detected. To this end, the Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 object computes the self capacitance single-ended measurement, and the Acquisition Configuration T8 object then triggers the recalibration.

Note that the SELFPROX bit in the Acquisition Configuration T8 MEASALLOW field must also be set for the self capacitance single-ended measurements to be used (see "MEASALLOW Field").

NOTE Self capacitance measurements must also be enabled for use in order for the self capacitance single-ended measurements to operate correctly. Therefore, the Auxiliary Touch Configuration T104 object must also be enabled for use.

#### 6.17.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-73: CONFIGURATION FOR SELF CAPACITANCE MEASUREMENT CONFIGURATION T113 (SPT_SELFCAPMEASURECONFIG_T113)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td></td><td>Reserved</td><td></td><td>DEFMEASIDLE</td><td>Reserved</td><td>ALTAXISEN</td><td>Reserved</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>XGAIN</td><td colspan="8">Gain for the X axis</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>YGAIN</td><td colspan="8">Gain for the Y axis</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Reserved</td><td colspan="8">Reserved</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>NODEAREASFCM</td><td colspan="8">Per node X/Y scaling factor - Calculated to Measured axis</td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>NODEAREASFMC</td><td colspan="8">Per node X/Y scaling factor - Measured to Calculated axis</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables the use of the Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 object. The object is enabled if set to 1, and disabled if set to 0.

NOTE A tune should be performed using the Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 object after enabling the Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 object (see "CMD Field").

ALTAXISEN: Specifies on which axis of electrodes to perform the single-ended self capacitance measurement.

If this bit is set to 0 , the measurement is performed on the X axis (that is, the axis that has the larger number of lines).

If this bit is set to 1, the measurement is performed on the Y axis (that is, the axis that has the smaller number of lines).

Note that setting ALTAXISEN should be done in conjunction with the Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 CTRL DISMEASX and DISMEASY controls if they are set.

DEFMEASIDLE: Setting this bit to 1 ensures that self capacitance single-ended measurements are included in the Default Measurement Types in Idle mode for use with Low Power Idle mode (see Section A.2.1 "Default Measurements").

Note that, regardless of the state of this bit, self capacitance single-ended measurements are always included in the Default Measurement Types for other processes (for example, Acquisition Configuration T8 recalibration) if the Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 object is enabled.

## XGAIN and YGAIN Fields

These fields set the X or Y axis gain, as appropriate, for the self capacitance single-ended measurement.

The default range is 0 to 29 and this should be sufficient for most applications. However, using Gain * 2 mode may help improve moisture immunity performance. To enable Gain * 2 mode, set XGAIN/YGAIN bit 7 to 1. This will add additional settings in the range to 128 to 157.

For more information on choosing a suitable gain value, refer to maXTouch U Series Tuning Guide.

Range: 0 to 29, 128 to 157 (Gain × 2 mode)

## NODEAREASFCM and NODEAREASFMC Fields

These fields specify the Node Area Scaling Factors for use with DC level estimation algorithm.

To save processing time, the DC estimation algorithm measures one axis to determine its DC level and then uses the results to calculate the DC level for the other axis. By default, the axis with the greater number of nodes is measured (that is, the X axis on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family), and the other (shorter) axis is calculated from this (that is, the Y axis). This can be changed, however, by setting the CTRL ALTAXISEN control to 1 (see "CTRL Field").

The scaling factors must be defined if the X and Y node areas differ, otherwise the calculated DC estimation will be incorrect. The NODEAREASFCM and NODEAREASFMC fields therefore specify the scaling factors to be used by the DC estimation algorithm in the form of two ratios:

- NODEAREASFCM specifies the ratio of the calculated axis area to the measured axis area; that is: \( \left( {{\mathrm{{Area}}}_{\mathrm{C}}/{\mathrm{{Area}}}_{\mathrm{M}}}\right) \)

- NODEAREASFMC specifies the reciprocal of NODEAREASFCM. This is the ratio of the measured axis area to the calculated axis area; that is: \( \left( {\mathrm{{Area}}}_{\mathrm{M}}\right. \) / \( {\mathrm{{Area}}}_{\mathrm{C}} \) ).

where \( {\mathrm{{Area}}}_{\mathrm{C}} \) is the calculated axis and \( {\mathrm{{Area}}}_{\mathrm{M}} \) is the measured axis.

NOTE The NODEAREASFCM and NODEAREASFMC fields are not independent of each other: they should be configured as a pair, with NODEAREASFMC set to the reciprocal value of NODEAREASFCM.

The actual calculation of the ratios depends on the setting of the CTRL ALTAXISEN control (see Table 6-74.

TABLE 6-74: NODEAREASF CORRECTION FACTOR

<table><tr><td></td><td colspan="2">Ratio Calculation</td></tr><tr><td>ALTAXISEN Setting</td><td>NODEAREASFCM</td><td>NODEAREASFMC</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>AreaY / Area</td><td>AreaX / AreaY</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>AreaX / AreaY</td><td>AreaY / AreaX</td></tr></table>

Note: Area \( {}_{X} = \) Total area of \( X \) electrodes,Area \( {}_{Y} = \) Total area of \( Y \) electrodes

The ratio specified in the NODEAREASFCM and NODEAREASFMC fields is specified in units of 1/128 minus 1, where the default value of 0 represents a value of 127 (that is, 128/128 = 1). For example:

---

\( {63} = \left( {{64}/{128}}\right)  = {0.5} \)

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;\( {127} = \left( {{128}/{128}}\right)  = 1 \)

\( {255} = \left( {{256}/{128}}\right)  = 2 \)

---

NOTE Values of 1 to 62 cannot be used, as the two fields are reciprocals of each other and the reciprocal values above 255 are not possible.

The maXTouch Studio tool can be used to calculate the values for these fields.

Range: 0 (127), 63 to 255

#### 6.17.3 CONFIGURATION CHECKS

The Self Capacitance Measurement Configuration T113 object causes a configuration check to be performed in the following circumstances:

- When the object is enabled (that is, the ENABLE bit is set in the CTRL field)

- If the object is enabled, when certain fields are changed

In addition, some fields will cause an automatic recalibration to be performed.

A configuration check may determine that a configuration error has occurred (for example, if a setting is set outside of its allowed range or a conflict has occurred between two settings). This is signaled to the host (see Section 3.3 "Command Processor T6 Object"). The device halts until the error has been corrected. To fix the error, check that all the object settings are within their allowed limits, as stated in the field descriptions.

TABLE 6-75: CONFIGURATION CHECKS FOR SELF CAPACITANCE MEASUREMENT CONFIGURATION T113

(SPT_SELFCAPMEASURECONFIG_T113)

<table><tr><td rowspan="2">Field</td><td colspan="2">Changing The Field Causes...</td><td rowspan="2">Effect of Configuration Checks On Field</td></tr><tr><td>Configuration Check</td><td>Automatic Recalibration</td></tr><tr><td>CTRL</td><td>Yes (1)</td><td>Yes</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>XGAIN</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>YGAIN</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>NODEAREASFCM</td><td>No</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr><tr><td>NODEAREASFMC</td><td>No</td><td>No</td><td>None</td></tr></table>

Note 1: If the ENABLE bit is toggled on or off.

### 6.18 Data Container T117 Object

#### 6.18.1 INTRODUCTION

The Data Container T117 objects are a set of read-only objects that together provide a mechanism for retrieving specific data from the device's internal memory. On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family, there are 6 instances of the Data Container T117 object and each instance holds 215 bytes, making 1290 bytes of data space in total. The multiple instances are concatenated so that the data is held in a contiguous manner across all the instances.

The data type is determined by the configuration of the Data Container Controller T118 object (see Section 6.19 "Data Container Controller T118 Object").

IMPORTANT! The CRC included by header type 128 is an 8-bit CRC only and therefore may not detect all the errors in the data that could be detected by a larger CRC. For this reason, the Data Container T117 and Data Container Controller T118 objects are not recommended for use in a UL/IEC 60730 Class B compliant product.

#### 6.18.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-76: CONFIGURATION FOR DATA CONTAINER T117 (SPT_DATACONTAINER_T117)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>DATA[0]</td><td colspan="8">Data byte 0</td></tr><tr><td colspan="10">...</td></tr><tr><td>214</td><td>DATA[214]</td><td colspan="8">Data byte 214</td></tr></table>

## DATA[] Fields

These fields contain the bytes of data, as determined by the Data Container Controller T118 object HEADERTYPE and DATATYPE fields (see "HEADERTYPE Field" and "DATATYPE Field").

IMPORTANT! On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family, if the DATA[] fields contain delta data, the deltas are output in big endian format (that is, MSByte first). All other data is output as standard little endian format (LSByte first).

On some other devices, however, the deltas may be output in standard little endian format (that is, LSByte first). Any generic host driver code will need to take this into account.

The data will extend across the DATA[] fields in the multiple instances of the Data Container T117 object in a contiguous manner. Any unused bytes are reserved.

NOTE On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family, there are a total of 1290 data bytes (split across 6 instances of 215 bytes each) and only those bytes needed to hold the data for the chosen Data Container Controller T118 Data Type are used. Any unused bytes in the DATA[] fields above the header and data are reserved and should not be processed by the host.

In addition, although the DATA[] fields include data for 640 possible nodes, on the mXT448UD-CCUBHA1 variant device, only a maximum of 448 nodes can be used on this device, so some of the bytes of data will represent unused nodes. These unused bytes may contain random data and should also be considered reserved.

For example, If the Data Container Controller T118 DATATYPE is 16 and the HEADERTYPE is 1, the DATA[] fields will contain a 1-byte header, followed by the 16-bit deltas for all the nodes in the sensor matrix. An example is shown in Figure 6-10.

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_251.jpg?x=235&y=217&w=1312&h=913&r=0"/>

The example shows nodes on the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1; on the mXT448UD-CCUBHA1 variant device there will be fewer nodes.

### 6.19 Data Container Controller T118 Object

#### 6.19.1 INTRODUCTION

The Data Container Controller T118 object provides configuration for the Data Container T117 object. The Data Container Controller T118 object makes internal data, such as deltas and references, available. The data type is selected in the Data Container Controller T118 object. There is no data processing, as the Data Container Controller T118 object simply gives direct access to internal data in memory. The internal data pointer is updated each acquisition during touch processing.

IMPORTANT! The CRC included by header type 128 is an 8-bit CRC only and therefore may not detect all the errors in the data that could be detected by a larger CRC. For this reason, the Data Container T117 and Data Container Controller T118 objects are not recommended for use in a UL/IEC 60730 Class B compliant product.

The following data types are available (see Table 6-78 for more information):

- Mutual Capacitance Deltas for all touchscreen nodes

- Mutual Capacitance References for all touchscreen nodes

A header that provides additional bytes at the start of data can also be selected (see the "HEADERTYPE Field"). The header is processed each acquisition during touch processing.

The data should not be accessed while it is being reloaded within the device. A message can be enabled to indicate when the data is safe to access and the header has been processed.

NOTE Data Container T117 and Data Container Controller T118 can generate a large volume of message traffic when enabled. This can interfere with systems that read the configuration at start-up (such as maXTouch Studio) or systems that check or upload the configuration as an anti-corruption check. It may be helpful to defer enabling Data Container Controller T118 until any start-up bus traffic is completed. This can be done by using a timer, triggered from Dynamic Configuration Controller T70 event ID 199.

#### 6.19.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-77: CONFIGURATION FOR DATA CONTAINER CONTROLLER T118

(SPT_DATACONTAINERCTRL_T118)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td colspan="6">Reserved</td><td>RPTEN</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>DATATYPE</td><td colspan="8">Data type</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>HEADERTYPE</td><td colspan="8">Header type</td></tr></table>

## CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables or disables the use of this object. The object is enabled if this bit is set to 1 , and disabled if this bit is set to 0 .

RPTEN: Enables or disables this object to report messages. Reporting is enabled if this bit is set to 1, and disabled if this bit is set to 0 .

## DATATYPE Field

This field selects the type of data to be used in the Data Container T117. See "DATA[] Fields" for an example of how DATATYPE helps populates the Data Container T117 DATA[] fields.

IMPORTANT! On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family, if the Data Container T117 DATA[] fields contain delta data, the deltas are output in big endian format (that is, MSByte first). All other data is output in standard little endian format (LSByte first).

## DATATYPE Field

This field outputs the data type (see Table 6-78). Invalid data types are output as zero.

## CRC Field

This 8-bit cyclic redundancy check (CRC) can be used to check the integrity of data. It is calculated over the header and the nodes specified in Multiple Touch Touchscreen T100 (see Section B.2 "8-bit CRC").

## TIMESTAMP Field

This 16-bit field outputs the timestamp in units of 16.384 KHz clock cycles (61.04 ms increments).

## CYCCNT Field

This 16-bit field outputs a Cycle Counter. The counter is incremented on each acquisition.

mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family 1.0

### 6.20 Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 Object

#### 6.20.1 INTRODUCTION

The Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 object can be used to configure the shape of the transition waveform for a self capacitance measurement.

The shape of the transition waveform for a self capacitance measurement is formed under the control of a Voltage Modulated Drive pulse. The Off and On times for the drive pulses are stored in a Drive Pulse table (see "DRVPULSE[] Fields") and these are used to shape the transition waveform.

On the mXT640UD-CCUBHA1 Family there are 2 instances of the Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 object, as follows:

- Instance 0 specifies the On and Off times for the positive pulse transitions on the rising edge (see Figure 6-11)

- Instance 1 specifies the On and Off times for the negative pulse transitions on the falling edge (see Figure 6-12)

- This allows for more control in matching the positive and negative transition waveforms.

##### 6.20.1.1 Voltage Modulation

Figure 6-11 shows the effect of Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 Instance 0 on the rising edge of the measurement waveform.

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_255.jpg?x=269&y=910&w=1374&h=879&r=0"/>

In figure Figure 6-11:

- The red lines show the default drive pulse (upper) and measurement waveform (lower).

- The blue lines show the voltage modulated drive pulse (upper) and measurement waveform (lower).

Note that both schemes have an automatic drive toggle at the start of the measurement.

In the case of Voltage Modulation, each drive pulse consists of a drive off time and a drive on time. A number of consecutive drive pulses may be used to shape the measurement waveform (up to a maximum of 20), as specified in the NUMDRVPULSES field. Note that the last drive pulse does not need to specify an on time and can be left at 0 (the minimum delay) to leave the drive on. In addition, there is a minimum off time, so if the Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 object specifies a shorter off time, this is extended to the minimum off time.

For a falling measurement waveform, as configured by Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 Instance 1, the logic is reversed, with the drive on time pushing the measurement waveform downwards. This is shown in Figure 6-12.

<img src="https://cdn.noedgeai.com/bo_d89ubaqlb0pc73cr34vg_256.jpg?x=277&y=326&w=1211&h=901&r=0"/>

NOTE If self capacitance measurements have pre-charge disabled, the second half (rounded up) of the negative pulse transition settings are also applied to the Y lines when transitioning from a mutual capacitance measurement to a self capacitance measurement. That is, the following DRVPULSE[] settings are applied:

((ROUND_UP(NUMDRVPULSES / 2)) - 1) to (NUMDRVPULSES - 1)

See the Self Capacitance Global Configuration T109 "CTRL Field" DISPRECHARGE control for details on disabling pre-charge.

#### 6.20.2 CONFIGURATION

TABLE 6-83: CONFIGURATION FOR SELF CAPACITANCE VOLTAGE MODULATION T133 (SPT_SELFCAPVOLTAGEMOD_T133)

<table><tr><td>Byte</td><td>Field</td><td>Bit 7</td><td>Bit 6</td><td>Bit 5</td><td>Bit 4</td><td>Bit 3</td><td>Bit 2</td><td>Bit 1</td><td>Bit 0</td></tr><tr><td>0</td><td>CTRL</td><td colspan="7">Reserved</td><td>ENABLE</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>CFG</td><td colspan="2">Reserved</td><td colspan="6">NUMDRVPULSES</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td rowspan="2">DRVPULSE[0]</td><td colspan="8">OFFTIME</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td colspan="8">ONTIME</td></tr><tr><td colspan="10">...</td></tr><tr><td>40</td><td rowspan="2">DRVPULSE[19]</td><td colspan="8">OFFTIME</td></tr><tr><td>41</td><td colspan="8">ONTIME</td></tr></table>

CTRL Field

ENABLE: Enables the use of this instance of the Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 object. The object is enabled if set to 1 , and disabled if set to 0 .

CFG Field

NUMDRVPULSES: Specifies the number of Drive Pulses to be used for self capacitance Voltage Modulation, up to a maximum of 20 (see "DRVPULSE[] Fields").

Each Drive Pulse has an Off time and On time for each stage of the modulation. Note that the state of the Drive will be On at the end of each Drive Pulse. Therefore, the last Drive Pulse in use can have an On time of 0, after which the drive will be left on anyway.

Note that Drive On is in an upwards direction for a rising edge (Instance 0) and a downwards direction for a falling edge (Instance 1) (see Figure 6-11 and Figure 6-12).

A value of 0 disables the functionality.

Range: 0 (disabled), 1 to 20

## DRVPULSE[] Fields

These fields specify the Drive Pulses for the voltage modulation.

OFFTIME and ONTIME: Specify the Off and On times for the drive pulse for this stage of the overall voltage modulation. The off or on time is specified in units of the CTE clock period (20 ns; 50 MHz).

Note that the device requires a few additional CTE cycles for essential processing, so the actual time will be slightly lengthened to allow for this. See the minimum off time in Figure 6-11 and Figure 6-12).

NOTE It is the user's responsibility to increase the integration time for each self capacitance instance in use in line with the increase in timing introduced by the Voltage Modulation drive pulses (see "INTTIME Field").

## OFFTIME/ONTIME Range: 0 to 255

#### 6.20.3 CONFIGURATION CHECKS:

The Self Capacitance Voltage Modulation T133 performs no configuration checks, although an automatic recalibration is performed whenever a field is changed.

TABLE 6-84: CONFIGURATION CHECKS FOR

SELF CAPACITANCE VOLTAGE MODULATION T133

(SPT_SELFCAPVOLTAGEMOD_T133)
